cause shown and after a full hearing before the Board of Trustees. Such hearing
shall be held after ninety (90) days' notice to the holder of the permit. After
a full hearing before the Board, the Board may, in its discretion, and for good
cause shown, revoke the permit granted thereby under the terms of this article.
The holder of the permit may appeal from the ruling of the Board directly to
the District Court of Woodward County, where the hearing shall be held de novo.
(2011 Code § 20-20)
CHAPTER 2
TREES AND SHRUBS
SECTION:
8-2-1: Definitions
8-2-2: Tree Board
8-2-3: Arborist Licensing Requirements
8-2-4: Authority Of Property Owner
8-2-5: Permit May Be Required
8-2-6: Street Tree Species Permitted
8-2-7: Planting Requirements And Restrictions
8-2-8: Tree Care Generally
8-2-9: Trimming Trees
8-2-10: Removal Of Dead Or Diseased Trees On Private Property
8-2-11: Injury To Trees And Shrubs Prohibited
8-2-12: Interference With Tree Board Prohibited
8-2-13: Review And Appeal Of Tree Board Decisions
8-2-1: DEFINITIONS:
When used in this chapter, the following words and terms shall have the
meanings ascribed to them in this section:
PARK TREES: Trees, shrubs, bushes and all other woody vegetation in public
parks having individual names and all areas owned by the Town or to which the
public has free access as a park.
STREET TREES: Trees, shrubs, bushes, and all other woody vegetation on land
lying between property lines on either side of all streets, avenues, or ways
within Town. (2011 Code § 1-80)
8-2-2: TREE BOARD:
   A.   Board Created; Members: There is hereby created and established a Town
Tree Board for the Town which shall consist of Town Board of Trustees, unless
appointed by the Mayor, with approval of the Board of Trustees. Said board
shall consist of no more than five (5) members. (2011 Code § 1-81)
   B.   Responsibilities: The Town Tree Board or its agent shall be responsible
for the planting, pruning, and removal of all trees located within the street
rights-of-way, easements, alleys and parks of the Town. (2011 Code § 1-83)
   C.   Compensation: Members of the board shall serve without compensation.
(2011 Code § 1-82)
8-2-3: ARBORIST LICENSING REQUIREMENTS:
   A.   License Required: It shall be unlawful for any person or firm to engage
in the business or occupation of trimming, pruning, treating, or removing
street or park trees within the Town without first applying for and procuring a
license. (2011 Code § 1-93)
   B.   License Fee: The license fee shall be as provided in the fee schedule
adopted by resolution of the Town Board of Trustees and shall be paid in
advance; provided, however, that no license shall be required of any public
service company or Town employee doing such work in the pursuit of his public
service endeavors. (2011 Code § 1-93; amd. 2017 Code)
   C.   Bond Requirements: Before any license shall be issued, each applicant
shall first file evidence of possession of liability insurance in the minimum
amounts of twenty five thousand dollars ($25,000.00) for bodily injury and five
thousand dollars ($5,000.00) for property damage indemnifying the Town or any
person injured or damaged resulting from the pursuit of such endeavors as
herein described. (2011 Code § 1-93)
8-2-4: AUTHORITY OF PROPERTY OWNER:
The owner of land abutting on any street may, when acting within the provisions
of this chapter, prune, spray, plant or remove trees in that part of the street
abutting his land not used for public travel. (2011 Code § 1-83)
8-2-5: PERMIT MAY BE REQUIRED:
A street tree permit shall be required only when the owner of property intends
to deviate from the rules and regulations contained in this chapter. (2011 Code
§ 1-83)
8-2-6: STREET TREE SPECIES PERMITTED:
The following list constitutes the official street tree species for the Town.
No species other than those included in this list may be planted as street
trees without written permission of the Town Tree Board.
Small trees:
Bradford pear
Flowering crabapple
Flowering dogwood
Hawthorn
Purple leaf plum
Redbud
Medium trees:
Bald cypress
Chinese pistachio
Golden raintree
Honey locust
Japanese pagoda tree
Kentucky coffee tree
Osage orange (male, thornless)
Pine oak
Red mulberry (male)
River birch
Large trees:
American sycamore
Black walnut
Burr oak
Chinese lacebark elm
Cottonwood (cotton less)
Green ash
Hackberry
London planetree
Pecan
Red oak
Silver maple (2011 Code § 1-84)
8-2-7: PLANTING REQUIREMENTS AND RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Spacing: The spacing of street trees will be in accordance with the
three (3) species size classes listed in section
8-2-6 of this chapter, and no trees may be planted closer together than the
following: small trees, thirty feet (30'); medium trees, forty feet (40'); and
large trees, fifty feet (50'). (2011 Code § 1-85)
   B.   Distance From Curb And Sidewalk: The distance trees may be planted from
curbs or curb lines and sidewalks will be in accordance with the tree species
size classes listed in section
8-2-6 of this chapter, and no trees may be planted closer to any curb or
sidewalk than the following: small trees, two feet (2'); medium trees, three
feet (3'); and large trees, four feet (4'). (2011 Code § 1-86)
   C.   Distance From Street Corners And Fire Plugs: No street tree shall be
planted closer than twenty feet (20') of any street corner, measured from the
point of nearest intersection curbs or curb lines. No street tree shall be
planted closer than ten feet (10') of any fire plug. (2011 Code § 1-87)
   D.   Small Trees Only Near Utility Line: No street trees other than those
species listed as small trees in section
8-2-6 of this chapter may be planted under or within ten (10) lateral feet of
any underground water line, sewer line, transmission line or other utility.
(2011 Code § 1-88)
8-2-8: TREE CARE GENERALLY:
The Town shall have the right to plant, trim, spray, preserve and remove trees,
plants, and shrubs within the lines of all streets, alleys, avenues, lanes,
squares and public grounds, as may be necessary to ensure safety when serving
Town utilities or to preserve the symmetry and beauty of such public grounds.
The Town Tree Board may remove, or cause or order to be removed, any tree or
part thereof which is in an unsafe condition or which, by reason of its nature,
is injurious to sewers, electric power lines, gas lines, water lines or other
public improvements, or other pest. (2011 Code § 1-89)
8-2-9: TRIMMING TREES:
   A.   1. Every owner of any tree overhanging any street or right-of- way
within the Town shall trim the branches so that such branches shall not
obstruct the light from any street lamp or obstruct the view of any street
intersection and so that there shall be a clear space of eight feet (8') above
the surface of the street or right-of-way. (2011 Code § 1-90)
      2.   Any owner or occupant who fails, refuses, or neglects to trim trees
and shrubbery as provided in subsection A1 of this section, after receiving
five (5) days' notice from the Town Code official or the Chief of Police to do
so, shall be guilty of an offense against the Town. Every day on which the
owner or occupant fails, refuses or neglects to trim such trees or shrubbery,
after the expiration of the five (5) days' notice, shall be a separate offense.
(2011 Code § 20-2)
   B.   The owners shall remove all dead, diseased or dangerous trees, or
broken or decayed limbs which constitute a menace to the safety of the public.
   C.   The Town shall have the right to trim any tree or shrub on private
property when it interferes with the proper spread of light along the street
from a streetlight, or interferes with visibility of any traffic control device
or sign, such trimming to be confined to the area immediately above the right-
of-way. (2011 Code § 1-90)
8-2-10: REMOVAL OF DEAD OR DISEASED TREES ON PRIVATE PROPERTY:
   A.   Authority: The Town shall have the right to cause the removal of any
dead or diseased trees on private property within the Town when such trees
constitute a hazard to life and property or harbor insects or disease which
constitute a potential threat to other trees within the Town.
   B.   Notice To Remove: The Town Tree Board will notify in writing the owners
of such trees.
   C.   Removal By Owner Or Town: Removal shall be done by the owners at their
own expense within sixty (60) days after the date of service of notice. In the
event of failure of owners to comply with such provisions, the Town shall have
the authority to remove such trees and charge the cost of removal on the owner
property tax notice. (2011 Code § 1-91)
8-2-11: INJURY TO TREES AND SHRUBS PROHIBITED:
It is unlawful for any person to injure any tree or shrubbery on any street or
alley in the Town. This section shall not prohibit the lawful and proper care
and removal of such trees and shrubbery. (2017 Code)
8-2-12: INTERFERENCE WITH TREE BOARD PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person to prevent, delay or interfere with the
Town Tree Board, or any of its agents or servants, while engaging in and about
the planting, cultivating, mulching, pruning, spraying, or removing of any
street trees, park trees, or trees on private grounds, as authorized in this
chapter. (2011 Code § 1-92)
8-2-13: REVIEW AND APPEAL OF TREE BOARD DECISIONS:
   A.   The Board of Trustees shall have the right to review the conduct, acts
and decisions of the Town Tree Board.
   B.   Any person may appeal from any ruling or order of the Town Tree Board
to the Board of Trustees who may hear the matter and make final decision. (2011
Code § 1-94)
CHAPTER 3
PARKS AND RECREATIONAL AREAS
SECTION:
8-3-1: Town Parks Designated
8-3-2: Park Use Prohibitions And Restrictions
8-3-3: Fees, Deposits And Regulations For Specific Facilities
8-3-4: Enforcement Officials
8-3-5: Violation; Penalty
8-3-1: TOWN PARKS DESIGNATED:
The following are the locations of public parks in the Town:
Lots One (1), Two (2), Three (3), Four (4), Five (5), and Six (6), and West 100
feet of Lots Eleven (11) and Twelve (12), in Block Thirteen (13), Original Town
of Mooreland, Oklahoma, According to record plat thereof.
A tract of land located in the NW1/4 of Block 18, in Original Town of
Mooreland, Oklahoma, according to the recorded plat thereof described by metes
and bounds as follows:
Beginning at NW corner of Block 18, thence East a distance of 240 feet, thence
South a distance of 150 feet, thence West a distance of 240 feet, thence North
a distance of 150 feet to the point of beginning; and Lots 1, 2, and 3 in Block
18 in Original Town of Mooreland, Oklahoma, according to the recorded plat
thereof; and a track of land located in the SW1/4 Block 20, in Original Town of
Mooreland, Oklahoma according to the recorded plat thereof, described by metes
and bounds as follows: Beginning at SW corner of Block 20, thence East a
distance of 240 feet, thence North a distance of 150 feet, thence West a
distance of 240 feet, thence South a distance of 150 feet to the point of the
beginning; and
Meyer Park being Reserve "A" of Meyer's Second Addition to the Town of
Mooreland, Oklahoma, according to the recorded plat thereof, dedicated by the
instrument record in Book 263 of Miscellaneous Records, at page 469, in the
office of the County Clerk of Woodward County, Oklahoma;
and shall be regulated by the provisions of this chapter. This chapter shall
regulate also all public parks of the Town which may, at any time, be acquired
or used as public parks by the Town. (2011 Code § 16-1)
8-3-2: PARK USE PROHIBITIONS AND RESTRICTIONS:
   A.   Discharging Firearms: No person shall discharge firearms in the public
parks. (2011 Code § 16-2)
   B.   Damaging Park Property:
      1.   No person shall write upon or mark or deface in any manner, or use
in any improper way, any water closet, park seat, building, fence, or other
property in any park. (2011 Code § 16-3)
      2.   No person shall break, cut, mutilate, injure, remove, or carry away
any trees, shrubs, plants, flowers, stone, stone walk, bench, chair, seat,
structure, fence, property, or anything whatsoever in, upon or near any park,
or any street, avenue, or highway around same. (2011 Code § 16-6)
      3.   No person may go or walk upon any space in the parks reserved for
flowers or other plants, or otherwise invade any plot reserved by the Town for
shrubbery, grass, or flowers, or for any other purpose. (2011 Code § 16-19)
   C.   Motor Vehicles And Traffic:
      1.   Use Of Roads Only: No person shall drive or ride upon the grass or
footways or walks or elsewhere than upon the roads provided for the use of
automobiles and other vehicles. (2011 Code § 16-4)
      2.   Compliance With Traffic Regulations: All automobiles, vehicles, and
equestrians, when meeting on the driveways in any park, shall keep to the right
and comply with all other requirements of this Code and the traffic ordinances
of the Town. (2011 Code § 16-15; amd. 2017 Code)
      3.   Speed Limit: No person shall drive or ride at a greater speed on
streets adjacent to a public park than fifteen (15) miles per hour. (2011 Code
§ 16-5)
      4.   Bicycles, Tricycles And Motorcycles: No person shall ride or drive a
bicycle, tricycle, or motorcycle in the parks, except upon the driveways
thereof; and when passing another vehicle or equestrian from the rear to the
front of such persons, shall pass to the left side and at a moderate rate of
speed. Bicycles, tricycles, and motorcycles may not travel more than two (2)
abreast. (2011 Code § 16-23)
      5.   Racing: Horse racing or racing with any automobile or other vehicle
is hereby prohibited in any park unless permission therefor is given by the
Mayor. (2011 Code § 16-22)
   D.   Animals:
      1.   Running At Large:
         a.   Prohibited Generally: No person shall permit any horse, cow, or
other domestic animal to go or run at large in the Town parks. All such animals
shall be taken up and impounded and, if not claimed within ten (10) days, shall
be sold as provided for the sale of animals impounded by this Code and the
ordinances of the Town; and the fact that such animals were found running at
large shall be evidence of permission therefor by the owners thereof. (2011
Code § 16-18; amd. 2017 Code)
         b.   Domestic Fowl: No person may permit any domestic fowl to run at
large in the parks unless permission therefor is granted by the Mayor. (2011
Code § 16-21)
      2.   Staking Animals: No person shall fasten any horse, cow, or other
animal to any tree, stake, building, post, or other fastening in any park.
(2011 Code § 16-14)
      3.   Hunting Or Trapping, Petting Park Animals: No person shall chase,
kill, set snares for, or pet any rabbit, squirrel, bird, fish, or any animal or
thing belonging to the parks or kept therein. (2011 Code § 16-9)
   E.   Nuisances Or Offensive Conduct:
      1.   No person shall commit any nuisance or any offense against decency
and good morals in a park. (2011 Code § 16-7)
      2.   No person shall curse, swear, or use abusive language, or fight,
throw stones, or behave in a riotous or disorderly manner in any park. (2011
Code § 16-11)
   F.   Disturbing Persons: No person may disturb or interfere with any picnic,
social gathering, or program of any group of persons. (2011 Code § 16-20)
   G.   Music, Speeches And Lectures: No person shall render any music, vocal
or instrumental, or deliver any oration, address, speech, sermon, or lecture in
any of the Town parks without permission from the Mayor. (2011 Code § 16-17)
   H.   Littering, Polluting Waters:
      1.   No person shall throw stones or rubbish of any kind into any lake,
pond, stream, or other place in the parks, except receptacles designated for
that purpose. (2011 Code § 16-8)
      2.   No person shall foul in any manner any spring or drinking fountain
or stream in any park. (2011 Code § 16-13)
   I.   Billposting: No person shall paste, affix, or inscribe any handbill,
poster, card, or device, or inscribe to or upon or against any fence,
structure, or property of or on any park or highway, street, or avenue
surrounding the same. (2011 Code § 16-10)
   J.   Fires: No person except park employees shall make a fire for any
purpose in the parks unless permission is given therefor by the Town Fire
Chief. This subsection shall not prohibit, however, fires for cooking purposes
in grills and fireplaces provided in said parks for such purposes. (2011 Code §
16-16)
   K.   Vending Stand: No person shall set up any booth, table, stand, or other
device for vending or retailing any candies, ice cream, or other article
whatsoever without first obtaining permission therefor from the Mayor or other
person authorized by him to grant such permission. (2011 Code § 16-12)
8-3-3: FEES, DEPOSITS AND REGULATIONS FOR SPECIFIC FACILITIES:
   A.   Swimming Pool: The Board of Trustees is authorized to operate, manage,
and control the swimming pool located in Mooreland Park. The Board of Trustees
shall fix the charge for use of the pool, by resolution, and establish
regulations concerning the use and operation of the pool and safeguards against
the spread of communicable diseases. (2011 Code § 16-25; amd. 2017 Code)
   B.   South Park Concession Stand: There shall be a deposit of seventy five
dollars ($75.00) for the use of the South Park concession stand upon obtaining
the key for the entrance to the concession stand. Upon returning the key, an
inspection of the facility will be performed by the utility foreman. To receive
a full refund of the deposit, the facility must have been properly cared for,
cleaned, hosed down with water and there shall be no damages to any part of the
property, equipment or premises. The bathrooms must have been maintained,
cleaned and hosed down with water, and all trash must be picked up and put in a
provided container for disposal. The deposit will be refunded in full, partial
or not at all, depending on the outcome of the inspection and return of the
key. (2011 Code § 16-26)
   C.   Mooreland Community Center:
      1.   Fee: The fee for the use of the Mooreland Community Center shall be
as provided in the fee schedule adopted by resolution of the Town Board of
Trustees. (2011 Code § 16-27; amd. 2017 Code)
      2.   Deposit: There shall be a one hundred dollar ($100.00) refundable
deposit paid at the time of checking out a key for the rent of the Community
Center. Upon returning of the key, an inspection of the facility will be
performed by Town personnel. All trash must be picked up, floors swept, kitchen
and bathrooms left clean and no destruction to any part of the building,
equipment or premises. The deposit will be refunded in full, partial, or not at
all depending on the outcome of the inspection. If the community building is to
be used on a weekend, the key must be obtained by five o'clock (5:00) P.M. in
the Town Hall on Friday before the weekend and returned by nine o'clock (9:00)
A.M. on the next working day upon completion of the use of the Community
Center. If not returned in a timely manner, an additional fee will be applied.
      3.   Rental Agreement: A rental agreement shall be approved by the Board
of Trustees with changes in the agreement being made by the Board of Trustees
as deemed necessary. (2011 Code § 16-27)
8-3-4: ENFORCEMENT OFFICIALS:
The keepers and watchmen of the parks shall be sworn in as special police and
are entrusted with the enforcement of the provisions of this chapter. They
shall at all times have assistance of the regular police force in enforcing the
same. (2011 Code § 16-24)
8-3-5: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall be guilty of a
misdemeanor and, upon conviction, shall be punishable as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. (Ord. 319, 3-14-2016)
CHAPTER 4
MOORELAND CEMETERY
SECTION:
8-4-1: Cemetery Established
8-4-2: Board Of Cemetery Trustees
8-4-3: Financial Duties Of Town Clerk-Treasurer
8-4-4: Cemetery Funds
8-4-5: Certificates Of Conveyance Of Lots Or Burial Sites; Abandonment
8-4-6: Fees
8-4-7: Memorials, Headstones, Landscaping And Maintenance
8-4-8: Violations; Penalty
8-4-1: CEMETERY ESTABLISHED:
The lands conveyed to the Town by deeds recorded in Book 240 of Miscellaneous
Records at pages 471 and 472, and replatted by plat recorded in Book 4 of Plats
at page 45, and Book 1262, pages 91 – 92 in the records of the County Clerk,
and any other such lands conveyed for such purpose, shall be and they hereby
are created and established as a Municipal cemetery under the laws of the State
of Oklahoma, and shall be known as "Mooreland Cemetery", which cemetery is
owned by and shall be operated by the Town as hereinafter set forth. (2011 Code
§ 6-1)
8-4-2: BOARD OF CEMETERY TRUSTEES:
   A.   Board Created: The Town Board of Trustees shall serve as the Board of
Cemetery Trustees for the Town having all the rights, privileges and duties
provided by statute for the Board of Cemetery Trustees. (2011 Code § 6-2)
   B.   Powers And Duties: The Town Board of Trustees shall have charge of and
control of the Mooreland Cemetery and is authorized to make rules and
regulations governing the management, improvement, and establishment of the
cemetery, and to fix the price for which lots shall be sold or for which an
interment shall be made; and the Board of Trustees shall appoint all officers
and employees necessary for the control and management of the cemetery,
including the appointment of a superintendent, whose duties shall be to care
for and protect the grounds and improvements thereon, enforce the rules and
regulations of the Board, supervise repairs and construction of improvements
and the maintenance of all permanent improvements and embellishments of any
kind tending to beautify the cemetery or preserve it permanently as a cemetery.
The employment compensation of all such employees shall be subject to the prior
approval of the Town Board of Trustees. (2011 Code § 6-3)
8-4-3: FINANCIAL DUTIES OF TOWN CLERK-TREASURER:
   A.   It shall be the duty of the Town Clerk-Treasurer, under the direction
of the Board of Trustees, to receipt for all monies received from the sale of
lots or from interments or from any other source, and to deposit such funds
with the Town Clerk- Treasurer as a Cemetery Fund. The Clerk-Treasurer shall,
on order of the Board of Trustees, pay out such funds for repairs, materials,
and services in the management, care and preservation of such cemetery. (2011
Code § 6-4)
   B.   The Town Clerk-Treasurer shall, on the first Monday in January and July
of each year, and at such other times as may be requested, make a full report
to the Town Board of Trustees of all lots sold, interments made, and all monies
received and expended by him in and about the cemetery. Monies shall be paid
out only on claims filed with and approved by the Board of Trustees and
warrants issued and signed by the Mayor and attested by the Town Clerk-
Treasurer. (2011 Code § 6-4; amd. 2017 Code)
8-4-4: CEMETERY FUNDS:
   A.   Cemetery Care Fund: There is hereby created a permanent fund to be
known as "the Cemetery Care Fund". Of all monies received from the sale of lots
and interments and paid to the Town Clerk- Treasurer, twelve and one-half
percent (12.5%) thereof shall be by him segregated, set aside and placed in the
fund. The fund shall be invested as provided by 62 Oklahoma Statutes section
348.1 under the direction of the Town Board of Trustees. The corpus of the
Cemetery Care Fund may be used only in purchasing lands adjacent to the
Mooreland Cemetery when the same are necessary therefor and as by State law
provides. The interest or income on the fund may be used in improving, caring
for and embellishing the lots, walks, drives, parks and other necessary
improvements on Mooreland Cemetery. (2011 Code § 6-5)
   B.   Perpetual Care Fund: Donations, deposits, or bequests may be made to
the Town Board of Trustees in trust for the special care of specified lots,
monuments, or mausoleums in the Mooreland Cemetery, and the funds shall be
segregated and set aside as a permanent fund to be known as the "Perpetual Care
Fund". A separate account shall be kept for each amount so deposited, donated
and bequeathed for the special care of specified lots. The Perpetual Care Fund
may be invested in like manner as the Cemetery Care Fund, and only the interest
derived from the fund shall be used in the care, maintenance and repair of such
lots, monuments, and mausoleums, unless otherwise specified by the donor. (2011
Code § 6-6; amd. 2017 Code)
   C.   General Cemetery Fund: There is hereby created a fund to be known as
the "General Cemetery Fund" for the Mooreland Cemetery. Of all the monies
received from the sale of lots and interments and paid to the Town Clerk-
Treasurer, eighty seven and one-half percent (87.5%) thereof shall be by him
placed in the General Cemetery Fund. All monies received from sale of other
services with respect to or in about the cemetery shall be placed in the fund.
Donations, gifts and bequests made to the Board of Trustees or to the Town not
in trust but for care and for current and/or annual special care of the
cemetery of specified lots, monuments, or mausoleums and any interest or income
therefrom shall be used by the Board in the current and/or annual expenses in
the improving, caring for and embellishing the lots, walks, drives, parks and
other necessary improvements and the care, maintenance and repair of lots
specified by the donor. (2011 Code § 6-7)
8-4-5: CERTIFICATES OF CONVEYANCE OF LOTS OR BURIAL SITES; ABANDONMENT:
It shall be the duty of the Mayor of the Town to sign all Certificates of
Conveyance of lots or burial sites in the Mooreland Cemetery, and it shall be
the duty of the Town Clerk- Treasurer to countersign or attest all such
certificates under the Seal of the Town, showing the price for which the lot or
lots are sold, specifying the name of the person to whom they are issued and
that he is the owner of the lot or lots described therein by number, as laid
down on the plat, for the purpose of interment; and such certificate shall vest
in the purchaser and his heirs a right in fee simple to such lot or lots, for
the sole purpose of interment.
   A.   Designation; Order Of Interment: The owner of a space may present his
or her deed to the Town Clerk-Treasurer designating in writing persons entitled
to be buried in the space or spaces owned. This designation may be amended at
any time by the owner in the same manner as the original designation. In the
event the owner fails to designate burial rights for the space or spaces owned,
and in the event the property is not transferred or conveyed as provided
herein, the right of interment in the space or spaces shall be in the following
order:
      1.   One space, niche or crypt shall be forever reserved for the owner
and one for the owner's surviving spouse, if any.
      2.   The remaining spaces shall pass to the heirs or devises of the owner
in the same manner as real property passes under Oklahoma law; provided,
however, that no person shall be interred in a space passing under this section
unless such person would have been eligible under the provision of this chapter
to be designated for burial in such space at the date of such person's death.
   B.   Rights Upon Interment: Whenever an interment of the remains of any
person is made in a space, the space thereby becomes inalienable and shall be
held as the space of the interred person. (Ord. 336, 5-14-2018)
8-4-6: FEES:
The costs for interments, cremations and plots shall be as provided in the fee
schedule adopted by resolution of the Town Board of Trustees. (2011 Code § 6-9;
amd. 2017 Code)
8-4-7: MEMORIALS, HEADSTONES, LANDSCAPING AND MAINTENANCE:
   A.   It shall be lawful for the owner of any lot(s) in the Mooreland
Cemetery to place on said lot(s) during the owner's life, permanent and
temporary memorials or other formations made of cement, artificial stone,
composition, or wood, provided said owner shall pay all actual costs of
placing, replacing, and removing said memorials and formations. Cemetery
workers shall be permitted to remove trees, plants, obstacles, bricks, or other
items which are deemed a hazard to the mowing area provided that Owners shall
remain responsible for maintenance of their lots and payment therefore.
   B.   Landscaping: Grass is the only permitted plot cover. Effective October
1, 2021, only Cemetery staff are permitted to plant, trim, or remove tree,
bushes, and flowering shrubs of any kind.
   C.   Maintenance by Lot Owner: Mowing and edging of individual site(s) by
lot owner will be permitted but will not hinder or restrict cemetery workers in
the performance of their duties. If individual site(s) are not mowed and edged
when cemetery workers are mowing and edging the same section, those areas will
be kept at the same level as the entire section by cemetery workers. Lot owner
may request to Cemetery Sexton that City maintenance equipment not be used for
the upkeep of their lot(s) unless determined necessary by the cemetery staff.
Cemetery Sexton will obtain contact information including, but not limited to,
contact name, address, city, state, zip, phone number (cell and residential),
and email address for owners requesting individual maintenance. Individual
maintenance contact information, changes, updates, and all other pertinent
information will be provided by the Cemetery Sexton to the City Hall Cemetery
Clerk for record keeping. Cemetery staff will provide and place one reflective
marker per plot (eliminate red flags) for each lot owner who submits a request
to the Cemetery Sexton that City maintenance equipment not be used for the
upkeep of their lot(s). Reflective marker will be placed by cemetery employees
at a predetermined location and height by the headstone. Reflective markers
will designate that contact(s) are responsible for the maintenance and upkeep
of the plot(s), excluding City employees from mowing and/or edging on that
location. This allowance does not give said contact permission to violate any
other cemetery ordinance. It is the contact's responsibility to properly
maintain the plot while not disturbing the reflective marker. If the reflective
marker is removed and not replaced, cemetery employees will assume upkeep.
Plastic flags or markers of any other kind are not permitted, except for the
designated reflective marker. It is ultimately the owner's responsibility that
all their lots with reflective markers are properly maintained. If any lot
becomes unsightly, the city cemetery staff will immediately assume
responsibility of upkeep. Cemetery workers shall be permitted to remove any
obstacle from a mowing area. Plastic flags, flowers or markers of any kind,
other than Memorial Day as described below, are not permitted with the
exception of plots with the designated reflective marker and items placed on
headstones or areas that do not interfere with mowers.
   D.   Special flowers and decorations will be permitted anywhere on a plot
for Memorial Day. Plot owners shall remove items they want to keep, after
Memorial Day. Any flowers placed upon cemetery plots shall be removed and
disposed of ten (10) days after Memorial Day each year. Reflective marker may
be excepted from the removal requirement. (2011 Code § 6-11; amd. Ord. 353, - -
2021)
8-4-8: VIOLATIONS; PENALTY:
Trespassing upon the ground of the Mooreland Cemetery or other violation or
desecration thereof, or any wilful violation of any of the rules and
regulations made by the Board of Trustees, shall be deemed a misdemeanor, and
any person convicted thereof shall be subject to penalty as provided by section
1-4-1 of this Code. (2011 Code § 6-10)
CHAPTER 5
SMOKING IN PUBLIC PLACES, MUNICIPAL PROPERTY, INDOOR AND OUTDOOR
SECTION:
8-5-1: Definitions
8-5-2: Possession Of Lighted Tobacco And Smoking Vape Devices In Certain Places
Prohibited
8-5-3: Exemptions
8-5-4: Designated Smoking Rooms And Areas
8-5-5: Posting
8-5-6: Violation And Penalty
8-5-7: Enforcement
8-5-1: DEFINITIONS:
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have
the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly
indicates a different meaning:
INDOOR AREA: Any enclosed area used or visited by employees or the public, at
all times, regardless of whether work is being performed. Indoor Area includes
work areas, employee lounges, restrooms, conference rooms, classrooms, employee
cafeterias, hallways, and other spaces used or visited by employees, as well as
all space between a floor and ceiling that is predorrunantly or totally
enclosed by walls or windows, regardless of doors, doorways, open or closed
windows, stairways, or the like.
MUNICIPAL PROPERTY: All building, Indoor Areas, and Outdoor Areas, including
but not limited to recreational areas, and other property, or portions thereof
owned or operated by the City of Mooreland, including, but not limited to
vehicles and equipment owned by the City.
OUTDOOR AREA: Any area that is not an indoor area, and includes most
recreational areas.
PUBLIC PLACE: Any enclosed indoor area where individuals other than employees
are invited or permitted; the term is synonymous with the phrase "any indoor
place used by or open to the public.
RESTAURANT: Any eating establishment regardless of seating capacity.
SMOKING: The carrying by a person of a lighted cigar, cigarette, pipe or other
lighted smoking device including vape product devices.
STAND-ALONE BAR, STAND- ALONE TAVERN, AND CIGAR BAR: An establishment that
derives more than sixty percent (60%) of its gross receipts, subject to
verification by competent authority, from the sale of alcoholic beverages and
low-point beer and no person under twenty-one (21) years of age is admitted,
except for members of a musical band employed or hired as provided in paragraph
2 of subsection B of Section 537 of Title 37 of the Oklahoma Statutes and that
is not located within, and does not share any common entryway or common indoor
area with, any other enclosed indoor area or workplace, including a restaurant;
TOBACCO PRODUCT: Any product that contains tobacco and is intended for human
consumption Tobacco Product does not include any product approved by the United
States Food and Drug Adrninistration for sale as a tobacco cessation product;
VAPE PRODUCTS: Any noncombustible product that may or may not contain nicotine
that employs a mechanical heating element, battery, electronic circuit, or
other mechanism, regardless of shape or size, that can be used to produce a
vapor in a solution or other form. Vapor Product shall include any vapor
cartridge or other container with or without nicotine or other form that is
intended to be used with an electronic cigarette, electronic cigar, electronic
cigarillo, electronic pipe, or similar product or device and any vapor
cartridge or other container of a solution, that may or may not contain
nicotine, that is intended to be used with or in an electronic cigarette,
electronic cigar, electronic cigarillo, or electronic device. (Ord. 347, 3-9-
2020)
8-5-2: POSSESSION OF LIGHTED TOBACCO AND SMOKING VAPE DEVICES IN CERTAIN PLACES
PROHIBITED:
   A.   The use of Tobacco and Vape Products is prohibited in all places where
the use of these products is prohibited by Oklahoma State Law.
   B.   The use of Tobacco and Vape Products is prohibited on all Municipal
Property, indoor and outdoor, including parks and recreational areas.
   C.   Nothing in this chapter prohibits any person or entity from prohibiting
the use of Tobacco and Vape products on their own property, even if the use of
these products is not otherwise prohibited in that area.
   D.   No person or entity shall knowingly permit the use of Tobacco and Vape
Products in an area that is under the control of that person or entity and in
which the use of Tobacco and Vape products is prohibited by law.
   E.   No person or entity shall permit the placement of ash receptacles, such
as ash trays or ash cans, within an area under the control of that person or
entity and in which the use of Tobacco and Vape products is prohibited by law.
However the presence of ash receptacles shall not be a defense to a charge of
the use of Tobacco and Vape products in violation of any provision of this
code.
   F.   No person shall dispose of Tobacco or Vape products in an area where
such use is prohibited. (Ord. 347, 3-9-2020)
8-5-3: EXEMPTIONS:
The restrictions provided in Section
8-5-2 shall not apply to the following:
   A.   Stand-alone bars, stand-alone taverns and cigar bars;
   B.   The room or rooms where licensed charitable bingo games are being
operated, but only during the hours of operation of such games;
   C.   Up to twenty-five percent (25%) of the guest rooms at a hotel or other
lodging establishment;
   D.   Retail tobacco stores predominantly engaged in the sale of tobacco
products and accessories and in which the sale of other products is merely
incidental and in which no food or beverage is sold or served for consumption
on the premises;
   E.   Workplaces where only the owner or operator of the workplace, or the
immediate family of the owner or operator, performs any work in the workplace,
and the work-place has only incidental public access. "Incidental public
access" means that a place of business has only an occasional person, who is
not an employee, present at the business to transact business or make a
delivery. It does not include businesses that depend on walk-in customers for
any part of their business;
   F.   Work-places occupied exclusively by one or more smokers, if the
workplace has only incidental public access;
   G.   Private offices occupied exclusively by one or more smokers;
   H.   Private residences and workplaces within private residences, except
that smoking shall not be allowed inside any private residence that is used as
a licensed child care facility during hours of operation;
   I.   Medical research or treatment centers, if smoking is integral to the
research or treatment;
   J.   A facility operated by a post or organization of past or present
members of the Anned Forces of the United States which is exempt from taxation
pursuant to Sections 501(c)(8), 501(c)(10) or 501(c)(19) of the Internal
Revenue Code, 26 U.S.C., Sections 501(c)(8), 501(c)(10) or 501(c)(19), when
such facility is utilized exclusively by its members and their families and for
the conduct of post or organization nonprofit operations except during an event
or activity which is open to the public; and
   K.   Any outdoor seating area of a restaurant; provided, smoking shall not
be allowed within fifteen (15) feet of any exterior public doorway or any air
intake of a restaurant.
   L.   Medical research or treatment centers, if smoking is integral to the
research or treatment. (Ord. 347, 3-9-2020)
8-5-4: DESIGNATED SMOKING ROOMS AND AREAS:
   A.   An employer not otherwise restricted from doing so under this article
may elect to provide smoking rooms where no work is performed except for
cleaning and maintenance during the time the room is not in use for smoking,
provided each smoking room is fully enclosed and exhausted directly to the
outside in such a manner that no smoke can drift or circulate into a nonsmoking
area. No exhaust from a smoking room shall be located within fifteen (15) feet
of any entrance, exit or air intake.
   B.   If smoking is to be permitted in any space exempted in Section 8-5-3 of
this article or in a smoking room pursuant to subsection (1) of this section,
such smoking space must either occupy the entire enclosed indoor space or, if
it shares the enclosed space with any nonsmoking areas, the smoking space shall
be fairy enclosed, exhausted directly to the outside with no air from the
smoking space circulated to any nonsmoking area, and under negative air
pressure so that no smoke can drift or circulate into a nonsmoking area when a
door to an adjacent nonsmoking area is opened. Air from a smoking room shall
not be exhausted within fifteen (15) feet of any entrance, exit or air intake.
Any employer may choose a more restrictive smoking policy, including being
totally smoke free.
   C.   A nursing facility licensed pursuant to the Nursing Home Care Act may
designate smoking rooms for residents and their guests. Such rooms shall be
fully enclosed, directly exhausted to the outside, and shall be under negative
air pressure so that no smoke can escape when a door is opened and no air is
recirculated to non-smoking areas of the building.
   D.   Restaurants shall be totally nonsmoking or may provide nonsmoking areas
and designated smoking rooms. Food and beverage may be served in such
designated smoking rooms, which shall be in a location which is fully enclosed,
directly exhausted to the outside, under negative air pressure so smoke cannot
escape when a door is opened, and no air is recirculated to nonsmoking areas of
the building. No exhaust from such room shall be located within fifteen (15)
feet of and entrance, exit or air intake. Such room shall be subject to
verification for compliance with the provisions of this subsection by the State
Department of Health. (Ord. 347, 3-9-2020)
8-5-5: POSTING:
   A.   The person who owns or operates a place where smoking, tobacco or vape
devise use is prohibited by law shall be responsible for posting a sign or
decal, at least four (4) inches by two (2) inches in size, at each entrance to
the building indicating that the place is smoke-free or tobacco-free. Where
smoking or tobacco use or vape devise use is prohibited in an outdoor area, a
weather resistant sign at least fifteen (15) inches by fifteen (15) inches in
size with lettering of at least one (1) inch shall be posted indicating that
the outdoor area is smoke-free or tobacco-free.
   B.   Responsibility for posting signs or decals shall be as follows:
      1.   In privately owned facilities, the owner or lessee, if a lessee is
in possession of the facilities, shall be responsible;
      2.   In corporately owned facilities, the manager and/or supervisor of
the facility involved shallbe responsible; and
      3.   In publicly owned facilities, the manager and/or supervisor of the
facility shall be responsible.
      4.   In or on municipal property, the City Manager or designee shall be
responsible. (Ord. 347, 3-9-2020)
8-5-6: VIOLATION AND PENALTY:
Any person who knowingly violates this chapter is guilty of a misdemeanor, and
upon conviction thereof, shall be punished by a fine of not less than ten
dollars ($10.00) nor more than one hundred dollars ($100.00). (Ord. 347, 3-9-
2020)
8-5-7: ENFORCEMENT:
The state or local government or the person who owns or operates a public place
shall, at a minimum, do the following in order to prevent smoking in public
places:
   A.   Post signs at entrances to places where smoking is prohibited which
state that smoking is prohibited or that the indoor environment is free of
tobacco or vape device smoke; and,
   B.   Ask smokers to refrain from smoking upon observation of anyone
violating the provisions of this act.
   C.   Any peace officer or code enforcement official may enforce this
chapter. (Ord. 347, 3-9-2020)
CHAPTER 6
AIRPORT HAZARDS AND OBSTRUCTIONS
SECTION:
8-6-1: Declaration
8-6-2: Definitions
8-6-3: Hazards And Obstructions Prohibited
8-6-4: Use Restrictions
8-6-5: Nonconformities
8-6-6: Material Changes
8-6-7: Existing Uses
8-6-8: Variances
8-6-9: Conflicting Provisions
8-6-10: Violation; Penalty
8-6-1: DECLARATION:
It is hereby determined that airport hazards and obstructions endanger the
life, health, safety and property of users of the Town of Mooreland Airport and
also if the obstruction types in effect reduce the size area available for
landing, taking off, and maneuvering of aircraft, thus tending to destroy or
impair the utility of the airport and the public investment therein.
Accordingly, it is declared:
   A.   The creation or establishment of an obstruction in the glide slope path
as set forth herein is a public nuisance and an injury to the region served by
the Town of Mooreland Airport.
   B.   In the interest of the public health, safety and general welfare of the
inhabitants of the State of Oklahoma that the creation or establishment of
obstructions or airport hazards should be prevented to alleviate the
destruction or impairment of the utility of the airport and the public
investment therein.
   C.   The prevention of hazards should be accomplished, to the extent legally
possible, by the exercise of the public power without compensation.
   D.   Both the prevention of the creation or establishment of airport hazards
and the elimination, removal, alteration, mitigation, or marking and lighting
of existing airport hazards are public purposes for which political
subdivisions may raise and expend public funds and acquire land or interests in
land. (2011 Code § 20-23)
8-6-2: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this chapter, unless the content otherwise requires, the following
words and terms shall have the following meanings:
AIRPORT: Town of Mooreland Airport, Mooreland, Oklahoma.
AIRPORT HAZARD: Any structure, tree, or use of land which obstructs the air
space required for or is otherwise hazardous to the flight of aircraft in
landing or taking off at the airport.
RUNWAY: The paved surface for landing and taking off of aircraft along its
length.
STRUCTURE: An object constructed or installed by man including, but without
limitation, buildings, towers, smokestacks, and overhead transmission lines.
TREE: Any object of natural growth. (2011 Code § 20-24)
8-6-3: HAZARDS AND OBSTRUCTIONS PROHIBITED:
It shall be unlawful for any person, firm, association, copartnership, or
corporation including the Town of Mooreland, a Municipal corporation, DBA Town
of Mooreland Airport, to construct, extend, or expand any structures which
would create an airport hazard or obstruction to the users of the Town of
Mooreland Airport, known as the glide slope path for approach to Runway 17 and
the glide slope path for approach to Runway 35. (2011 Code § 20-25)
8-6-4: USE RESTRICTIONS:
Absent regulation of airport hazards and obstructions in the vicinity of the
airport, there is a possibility that uses could be permitted which endanger
safe aircraft operations. The land area owned by the Town of Mooreland, DBA
Town of Mooreland Airport, is hereby designated for glide slope paths for
approach to Runway 17 and approach to Runway 35. Notwithstanding any other
provision of this chapter, no use shall be made of land within any glide slope
path established by this chapter in such a manner as to:
   A.   Release into the air any substance which would impair visibility or
otherwise interfere with the operation of aircraft, e.g., steam, dust, smoke;
   B.   Produce light emissions, either direct or indirect (reflective), which
would interfere with pilot vision;
   C.   Produce emissions which would interfere with aircraft communication
systems or navigational equipment;
   D.   Attract birds or water fowl such as, but not limited to, operation of
sanitary landfills, maintenance of feeding stations, or the procuring of
certain vegetables; and/or
   E.   Introduce any use which would endanger the landing, taking off, or
maneuvering of aircraft. (2011 Code § 20-26)
8-6-5: NONCONFORMITIES:
The regulations prescribed by this chapter shall not be construed to require
the removal, lowering, or other changes or alteration of any structure or tree
not conforming to the regulations as of the effective date hereof or otherwise
interfere with the continuance of any nonconforming use. Nothing herein
contained shall require any change in the construction, alteration, or intended
use of any structure, the construction or alteration of which was begun prior
to the effective date hereof, and is diligently prosecuted. (2011 Code § 20-27)
8-6-6: MATERIAL CHANGES:
No material change shall be made in the use of the land, and no structure or
tree (natural growth) shall be erected, altered or otherwise established in the
glide slope path. (2011 Code § 20-28)
8-6-7: EXISTING USES:
There shall be no allowance granted that would permit the establishment or
creation of an airport hazard or permit a structure or tree to be made or
become higher, or become a greater hazard to air navigation, than it was on the
effective date hereof, or any amendments hereto. Except as indicated, all
applications for such a permit shall be granted. (2011 Code § 20-29)
8-6-8: VARIANCES:
Any variance may, if such action is deemed advisable to effectuate the purpose
of this chapter and be reasonable in the circumstances, be granted. (2011 Code
§ 20-30)
8-6-9: CONFLICTING PROVISIONS:
Where there exists a conflict as prescribed in this chapter and any other
regulation applicable to the same area, whether the conflict be with respect to
the height of structures or trees, the use of land, or other matter, the more
stringent limitation or requirement shall govern and prevail. (2011 Code § 20-
31)
8-6-10: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person who violates or fails to comply with any provision of this chapter,
or any legal order or regulation made pursuant hereto, shall be guilty of a
misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be punishable as provided in
section
1-4-1 of this Code. Each day upon which a violation continues shall be deemed a
separate offense. (2011 Code § 20-32)
CHAPTER 7
RAILROADS
SECTION:
8-7-1: Improvements To And Maintenance Of Public Ways
8-7-2: Trains Obstructing Crossings
8-7-3: Climbing On Moving Train
8-7-4: Loitering On Railroad Premises
8-7-5: Violation, Penalties And Costs
8-7-1: IMPROVEMENTS TO AND MAINTENANCE OF PUBLIC WAYS:
   A.   Streets:
      1.   When the tracks of any railroad company cross any street that is
being or has been paved, the company shall pave as much of the street as is
occupied by its track or tracks and two feet (2') on each side, using the same
material as is to be or has been used on the street, or such other satisfactory
material as the Town Board of Trustees, by motion or resolution, may approve.
      2.   When more than one (1) track crosses a street within a distance of
one hundred feet (100'), measuring from inside rail to inside rail, the
railroad company shall grade, gutter, drain, and curb the street area between
its tracks, and surface or pave it with the same material which the Town is to
use or has used on the street.
      3.   Railroad companies shall keep all such improvements made by them in
a good state of repair at all times. (2011 Code § 21-30)
   B.   Sidewalks:
      1.   Railway companies shall construct sidewalks crossing their rights-
of-way, using the same materials as are used in the adjacent sidewalks insofar
as this is practicable under the circumstances.
      2.   They shall construct sidewalks on both sides of the streets when
both sides are used by pedestrians.
      3.   The company shall keep such sidewalks in good state of repair at all
times. (2011 Code § 21-31)
8-7-2: TRAINS OBSTRUCTING CROSSINGS:
It is unlawful for the directing officer or person in charge of any railroad
train or railroad car to direct the operation of or to operate the same in such
manner as to prevent the use of any street for purposes of travel for a period
of time longer than five (5) minutes. (2011 Code § 21-32)
8-7-3: CLIMBING ON MOVING TRAIN:
It is unlawful for any person to climb upon, hold to, or in any manner attach
himself to any railway train, locomotive, or railway car while such is in
motion within the Town, unless such person is acting in the line of duty. (2011
Code § 21-33)
8-7-4: LOITERING ON RAILROAD PREMISES:
It is unlawful for any person not acting within the line of duty, not having
any proper business or not being on any proper mission requiring his presence
there, to loiter within a railroad station or other railway building, upon a
railroad station platform, or anywhere upon a railroad yard or other railroad
premises. (2011 Code § 21-34)
8-7-5: VIOLATION, PENALTIES AND COSTS:
   A.   Violation; Penalties: Any person, firm or corporation who violates any
provision of this chapter shall be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon
conviction, shall be punishable as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. The penalty may not be greater than that established by
statute for the same offense. (2011 Code § 21-36; amd. 2017 Code)
   B.   Court Costs: The Municipal Court shall assess court costs in all
matters in which an offender is found guilty or pleads guilty or no contest to
the offense. Such costs shall be set at the maximum amount allowed by the State
legislature. (Ord. 325, 8-8-2016)
TITLE 9
PUBLIC UTILITY SERVICES
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL ADMINISTRATIVE PROVISIONS
SECTION:
9-1-1: Application Of Provisions
9-1-2: Administrative Authority
9-1-3: Billing And Billing Adjustments
9-1-4: Discontinuance Of Service; Disconnect And Reconnect Fees
9-1-5: Lien Imposed
9-1-6: Violation; Penalty
9-1-1: APPLICATION OF PROVISIONS:
The provisions of this title shall apply to the public utilities of the Town,
being its electric distribution system, its water system, its sanitary sewer
system and its garbage and refuse disposal and collection system. (2011 Code §
19-81; amd. 2017 Code)
9-1-2: ADMINISTRATIVE AUTHORITY:
The Town Administrator shall have the authority to decide any questions
contained in this title, and his decision in such cases shall become final
unless appealed to the Board of Trustees. (2011 Code § 19-85; amd. 2017 Code)
9-1-3: BILLING AND BILLING ADJUSTMENTS:
   A.   Rendition Of Bills:
      1.   The Town may mail a bill for service to the consumer at the address
at which service is taken or such other address as designated by the customer;
however, the Town reserves the right to adopt other methods for delivery of
bills.
      2.   Delivery is deemed to have taken place when, according to the Town's
records, a bill or any notice containing billing or past due information has
been properly delivered to the U.S. Postal System.
      3.   Failure to receive a bill in no way exempts a customer/consumer from
liability for payment of services. (2011 Code § 19-109)
   B.   Late Payment Charge: There is hereby created a late charge for the
delinquent payment of bills due the Town for sewer, trash, water and
electricity charges. The penalty shall be ten percent (10%) of the total
monthly sewer, trash, electricity and water bill, and the Town Clerk-Treasurer
shall assess the late charge to all bills which are not paid on or before the
tenth day from the billing date printed on the bill. The due date shall be no
sooner than ten (10) days after the bill is mailed. (2011 Code §§ 19-82, 19-
110)
   C.   Authority To Adjust Accounts: In cases of either an undercharge or an
overcharge to a utility customer's account, the Town Board of Trustees hereby
authorizes the Town Administrator and appointed Mooreland Public Works
Authority Clerk to adjust a utility customer's account to reflect an accurate
and correct account balance. (2011 Code § 1-39; amd. 2017 Code)
9-1-4: DISCONTINUANCE OF SERVICE; DISCONNECT AND RECONNECT FEES:
In the event any customer shall fail to pay his utility bill on or before the
twentieth day of the month in which it is due, the water service, the electric
service and the garbage service to such customer shall be discontinued
forthwith and without notice, and a fee set and established by resolution of
the Board of Trustees of the Mooreland Public Works Authority and approved and
adopted by resolution of the Town Board of Trustees, and posted for inspection
in the Office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer shall be entered against the account
of the customer. Water service, electric service and/or garbage service to any
such discontinued account or customer shall not be reinstated or resumed until
all such sums due the Town, all indebtedness of all kinds, together with said
fee, shall have been paid in full. Reconnection after hours or on holidays
shall incur a fee set and established by resolution of the Board of Trustees of
the Mooreland Public Works Authority and approved and adopted by resolution of
the Town Board of Trustees, and posted for inspection in the Office of the Town
Clerk-Treasurer. (2011 Code § 19-83; amd. 2017 Code)
9-1-5: LIEN IMPOSED:
In addition to any other remedy provided herein for the enforcement of
collection of any utility rate or charge made under the provisions of this
title, all rates provided in this title shall be a lien against the premises to
which said utility service may be supplied, and the owners thereof and
occupants shall be severally responsible to the Town in an action waged by the
Town in any court of competent jurisdiction for the amount of all such rates
and charges as may be due and unpaid, together with all penalties provided
herein and costs. (2011 Code § 19-84)
9-1-6: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person, firm, association, or corporation who shall violate any of the
provisions of this title shall be deemed guilty of an offense and, upon
conviction thereof, shall be punishable as provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. A separate offense shall be deemed committed upon each day
during or on which a violation occurs or continues. (2011 Code § 19-120)
CHAPTER 2
TERMS AND CONDITIONS OF UTILITY SERVICES
SECTION:
9-2-1: Scope
9-2-2: Application Of Provisions; Noncompliance
9-2-3: Amendments
9-2-4: Continuity And Quality Of Service
9-2-5: Nonliability Of Town For Water Leaks; Maintenance Of Pipes And Fixtures
9-2-6: Denial Of Service
9-2-1: SCOPE:
This chapter shall govern billing and collection for the Town's utility
services. They supersede and cancel all previous terms and conditions of
service or portions thereof that pertain to the billing and collection for
utility services. (2011 Code § 19-90)
9-2-2: APPLICATION OF PROVISIONS; NONCOMPLIANCE:
   A.   This chapter and any modifications thereof and additions thereto
lawfully made are applicable to all consumers receiving utility service from
the Town, and to all existing contracts which may be entered into by the Town,
and to all rate schedules which, from time to time, may be lawfully
established.
   B.   The Town may decline to serve a consumer or prospective consumer until
such consumer has complied with the rules and regulations of the Board of
Trustees of the Mooreland Public Works Authority and any applicable Federal,
State, and Municipal or other local laws, rules and regulations.
   C.   The Town may refuse or discontinue service to any consumer for
noncompliance with this chapter where they specifically so provide. (2011 Code
§ 19-91)
9-2-3: AMENDMENTS:
The Town retains the right to amend this chapter or to make additional terms
and conditions of service as it may deem necessary. (2011 Code § 19-92)
9-2-4: CONTINUITY AND QUALITY OF SERVICE:
   A.   The Town will use reasonable diligence to supply continuous service at
the point of delivery in all systems. It shall be the responsibility of the
consumer to install and maintain protective devices which will protect the
consumer's equipment and processes during abnormal service conditions or the
failure of part or all of a service. In no event will the Town be liable for
any service interruptions, irregularities, or any other causes or abnormalities
not caused by the sole negligence of the Town. (2011 Code § 19-93)
   B.   In order to make repairs to or changes in the Town's facilities for
supplying service, the Town reserves the right, without incurring any liability
therefor, to suspend service without notice to the consumer for such periods as
may be reasonably necessary. When conditions permit, an attempt will be made to
notify consumers affected by such an interruption. Insofar as is practicable,
interruptions shall be scheduled at a time which will cause the least
reasonable inconvenience to consumers, and where feasible, consumers likely to
be seriously affected (e.g., installations affected with interest of public
health and safety) will be notified in advance.
   C.   The Town also reserves the right to discontinue service without advance
notice when a defective condition of equipment or wiring upon the premises of
the consumer results, or is likely to result, in danger to life or property, or
interference with proper service to others. Service(s) will not be resumed
until the dangerous condition has been remedied to the satisfaction of the
Town. If such condition is the result of tampering with the Town equipment, the
provisions of this chapter shall also apply. (2011 Code § 19-93; amd. 2017
Code)
9-2-5: NONLIABILITY OF TOWN FOR WATER LEAKS; MAINTENANCE OF PIPES AND FIXTURES:
The Town will not be liable for any loss, damage or injury whatsoever caused by
leakage, escape or loss of water after same has passed through the meter, nor
for defects in the customer's piping or fittings. All pipes and fixtures on the
premises side of the meter shall be kept in good repair and free from leaks at
the expense of the customer/consumer and not of the Town. (2011 Code § 19-94)
9-2-6: DENIAL OF SERVICE:
The Town reserves the right to refuse to provide service to a consumer at any
premises until all delinquent bills for prior or current utility service
incurred with the Town are paid. The Town shall not be required to provide
service to a consumer who uses an alias, trade name, or business name of a
relative or another person as a device to escape payment of an unpaid
obligation for prior service. (2011 Code § 19-95)
ARTICLE A. APPLICATIONS AND DEPOSITS FOR SERVICES
SECTION:
9-2A-1: Application For Services; Fees
9-2A-2: Special Contract
9-2A-3: Separate Applications Required
9-2A-4: Nontransferability Of Service
9-2A-5: Responsibility For Changes In Service
9-2A-6: Service Deposits
9-2A-7: Termination Of Service
9-2A-8: Occupancy Without Application Or Deposit
9-2A-1: APPLICATION FOR SERVICES; FEES:
   A.   Application Requirements: Each customer/consumer desiring electricity,
water, sewer and/or sanitation service from the Town shall make written
application to the Town Clerk-Treasurer located at 214 S. Main Street in the
Town of Mooreland. The account will be placed in the name of the person who
signs the application for service, and that applicant shall be considered the
party responsible for the account. This application shall contain the true name
of the applicant, date of birth, service and mailing addresses (if different),
telephone number, social security number, employer, next of kin not residing at
the same address, and such other information as the Town may deem necessary in
order to ensure the effective billing and collection of each account applied
for. Identification proving that the applicant is at least eighteen (18) years
of age must be presented when the application is filed, including a legible,
valid copy of the existing lease in the case of a renter/tenant applying for
service. Refusal to provide any requested information or providing false
information may result in denial or termination of service. (2011 Code §§ 4-14,
19-96)
   B.   Deposit And Connection Fees: The necessary deposit shall be made at the
time of application. The Town will have the premises inspected and, if in
conformance with this chapter and service and applicable provisions of this
Code, the application shall be approved and the necessary connections and
installations shall be made. A connection fee will be collected at the time
deposits are made for services with the Town. Said fee will be as set and
established by resolution of the Board of Trustees of the Mooreland Public
Works Authority and approved and adopted by resolution of the Town Board of
Trustees, and posted for inspection in the Office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer.
   C.   Tap Fees: In addition to connection fees, a tap fee will be collected
at the time deposits are made for services with the Town. Said fees shall be as
set and established by resolution of the Board of Trustees of the Mooreland
Public Works Authority and approved and adopted by resolution of the Town Board
of Trustees, and posted for inspection in the Office of the Town Clerk-
Treasurer. (2011 Code §§ 4-14, 19-96; amd. 2017 Code)
   D.   Recordkeeping: All applications, deposits, and fees required in this
section shall be deposited with and made of record in the Office of the Town
Clerk-Treasurer. (2011 Code §§ 4-14, 19-96)
9-2A-2: SPECIAL CONTRACT:
The Town may require a contract over an extended period of time when a
consumer's requirements for power or energy are unusually large or necessitate
considerable special or reserve equipment; and in such cases, may require
payment by the consumer of such charges and amounts in addition to the
prevailing rate schedule as may be necessary to justify the investment of the
Town. Arrangements for contracts will be made between the customer and the
appropriate utility director. (2011 Code § 19-97)
9-2A-3: SEPARATE APPLICATIONS REQUIRED:
A single application for service cannot be made to apply to different locations
nor to cover more than one (1) point of delivery at the same location to be
used by the same consumer, unless the Town determines that the physical
characteristics of the facility served requires more than one (1) point of
delivery according to good engineering and operating practices. Such
determination shall be made by the appropriate utility director. (2011 Code §
19-98)
9-2A-4: NONTRANSFERABILITY OF SERVICE:
An application and contract for service is not transferable from one (1)
consumer to any other consumer. Service can be connected for the same consumer
moving from one (1) address to another by the completion of a new application
and by a new deposit. Such application must be completed in the Office of the
Town Clerk- Treasurer. Service will not be connected if, on the date for which
the connection is requested, there exists or will exist any past due balance on
the account after the existing deposit amount has been applied. (2011 Code §
19-99)
9-2A-5: RESPONSIBILITY FOR CHANGES IN SERVICE:
It is the responsibility of the customer/consumer to notify the Town of any
changes in occupancy that will substantively affect the billing and/or service
of the customer/consumer. Changes may be requested in person, in writing or by
telephone. Any request for service requiring installation must be accompanied
by a signed application and a new deposit, the amount of which will be
determined according to subsection 9-2A-6C of this article. The Town will not
be held responsible for any error or omission in account changes if said
changes are not made in person. (2011 Code § 19-100)
9-2A-6: SERVICE DEPOSITS:
   A.   Required: Every potential customer/consumer making application for
utility service with the Town shall make a deposit. There shall be a deposit
made for every application for service and for each separate premises, except
as may be otherwise specified in this chapter.
   B.   Management And Use Of Deposits: Utility deposits shall be held by the
Town Clerk-Treasurer. In the event any customer/consumer should desire to
discontinue service or becomes no longer active, the Town Clerk-Treasurer is
hereby authorized to credit the customer's/consumer's account in the amount of
the deposit made. However, if the meter or meters located on the premises are
damaged in any way except by ordinary wear, as ascertained by the appropriate
utility director, the whole of the deposit, or as much thereof as is necessary
to pay the amount due the Town, shall be deducted from the deposit. (2011 Code
§ 19-101)
   C.   Deposits Established:
      1.   Residential Deposits: For purpose of guaranteeing payment of the
monthly utility bill, a residential deposit in accordance with the following
schedule shall be made at the time application is made with the Town Clerk-
Treasurer:
         a.   Water and sewer: Twenty dollars ($20.00).
         b.   Electric:
            (1)   Good credit - letter of credit from previous utility supplier
or good credit with the Town: Seventy five dollars ($75.00).
            (2)   Minimum credit - no letter of credit from previous utility
supplier or occasional slowness in payment: One hundred twenty five dollars
($125.00).
            (3)   Maximum credit - judgments, bankruptcy, charge offs, etc., or
refusal to obtain a credit report from previous utility supplier: Two hundred
dollars ($200.00). (2011 Code § 19-102)
      2.   Commercial Deposits: For purpose of guaranteeing payment of the
monthly utility bill, a commercial deposit in accordance with the rate schedule
set and established by the Board of Trustees of the Mooreland Public Works
Authority, approved and adopted by the Town Board of Trustees, and posted for
inspection in the Office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer, shall be made at the time
application is made with the Town Clerk-Treasurer. The commercial electric
deposit shall be one hundred dollars ($100.00). (2011 Code § 19-103)
   D.   Exemptions: Federal, State and local governmental agencies shall be
exempt from making deposits with the Town. Public schools shall also be
classified as exempt from making deposits. (2011 Code § 19-105)
   E.   Unclaimed Deposits: If, after termination of all services on an
account, deposit amounts remain as a credit balance after all debits, credits
and interest have applied or if any other credit balance remains, after one (1)
year, the Town Clerk-Treasurer shall send written notice to the customer at the
last known address for the customer, stating that the deposit or credit balance
shall become the property of the Town and be deposited by the Town Clerk-
Treasurer into the general fund, unless it is claimed by the customer within
ninety (90) days of the date that the notice is mailed by the Town. (2011 Code
§ 19-106)
9-2A-7: TERMINATION OF SERVICE:
   A.   When a customer elects to terminate service, the customer shall
promptly notify the Town in person, by telephone or in writing as to the
proposed effective date and hour of liability for payments for subsequent
services at that service address. The Town may disconnect service at any time
after eight o'clock (8:00) A.M. on the day for which discontinuation is
requested. If service has been disconnected in accordance with the customer's
previously stated request, but the customer subsequently requests the service
to be temporarily reconnected for any reason, an additional service call charge
set and established by resolution of the Board of Trustees of the Mooreland
Public Works Authority and approved and adopted by resolution of the Town Board
of Trustees, and posted for inspection in the Office of the Town Clerk-
Treasurer must be paid in cash and a new disconnect date must be rescheduled
prior the reconnection of services. (2011 Code §§ 19-107; amd. 2017 Code)
   B.   The Town will read the appropriate meter on the date for which
termination of service is requested and may, at its option, disconnect the
service. A final bill will be prepared as a result of the final reading. The
deposit will be applied to the final bill. The Town will not be held
responsible for any error or omission in termination of service if such request
is not made in person. (2011 Code § 19-107)
9-2A-8: OCCUPANCY WITHOUT APPLICATION OR DEPOSIT:
If the Town leaves the service connected to vacant premises, it does not
constitute consent by the Town for any new occupant of such premises to use the
service without making proper application for said service. Occupants using
service without deposit and/or application shall be liable to the Town for the
deposit amount, as well as payment for all services received, which will be
billed at the prevailing rates for all services available to the premises. Said
occupant will be required to show a lease or document specifying when occupancy
began and will be billed back to the reading nearest to the date of the last
tenant moving out. Failure to make application and/or deposit will result in
immediate termination of service. (2011 Code § 19-108)
ARTICLE B. CREDIT AND COLLECTION POLICIES
SECTION:
9-2B-1: Discontinuance Of Services
9-2B-2: Termination Of Service
9-2B-3: Dishonored Checks
9-2B-4: Payment Extensions
9-2B-5: Summary Of Policies After Posted Notice
9-2B-6: Summary Of Collection Policies
9-2B-1: DISCONTINUANCE OF SERVICES:
   A.   Charges for utility services shall be due and payable monthly according
to dates to be determined by the Town. Each monthly bill shall have printed
thereon the due date. In addition to the assessment of any late payment charge,
if a monthly bill is not paid by the due date indicated thereon, the account
shall be subject to disconnection for nonpayment. Utility service shall be
discontinued for any customer/consumer who owes any past due amount for utility
services or any charges for utility services, including late payment charges.
(2011 Code § 19-111; amd. 2017 Code)
   B.   The Town may discontinue utility service to a customer/consumer for the
reasons set forth below. Disconnect may take place at any time during normal
working hours on the day designated for disconnect. Notification of impending
discontinuation of service shall be given at the premises, either by letter,
"door knocker" or such other notification as the Town deems necessary and
appropriate. Failure to accept or acknowledge notification shall not be cause
for delay of the disconnection.
      1.   Nonpayment of a bill, or any portion of a bill, including any bill
for service rendered by the Town to the consumer at any premises for any
utility service.
      2.   Refusal by the consumer to provide the Town reasonable access to its
equipment upon the consumer's premises in accordance with this chapter.
      3.   Violation of any rule or regulation of the Town or noncompliance
with any applicable Federal, State, Municipal or other local laws, rules or
regulations.
      4.   Failure of the consumer to make application and place a deposit for
service.
      5.   Failure of the consumer to make application for utility service in
the true name of the consumer for the purpose of avoiding payment of an unpaid
obligation for utility service provided.
      6.   Returned checks.
      7.   Failure of the consumer, upon request, to provide the Town with a
deposit; provided, in no event shall service be discontinued for failure to
post a deposit earlier than twenty (20) days after demand has been made for
such deposit.
   C.   The Town may discontinue utility service without advance notice to a
consumer for any of the reasons set forth below, but notice will be posted at
the premises at the time of discontinuance of service, indicating the reason
for the disconnection:
      1.   Existence of a dangerous or defective condition of wiring or
equipment on the consumer's premises.
      2.   Fraudulent use of electricity or water.
      3.   Tampering with the Town's regulating and measuring equipment or
other property.
      4.   Expiration of the temporary utility service agreement.
      5.   Failure to comply with the terms of an extension agreement. (2011
Code § 19-111)
9-2B-2: TERMINATION OF SERVICE:
   A.   At least five (5) days' notice shall be given to a customer that
utility service will be terminated. Said notice shall be a separate final
notice and shall state the balance due, the date service will be terminated,
inform the customer of the proposed termination and his right to a hearing
before a Utility Service Committee, which will be made up of a member of the
Town Board of Trustees, appointed by the Town Board of Trustees and the Town
Administrator and/or the Town Clerk-Treasurer. Said notice shall be sent prior
to the actual cutoff date and provide that the customer may contact the Town
offices requesting a hearing. The hearing is the right of the customer, and a
meeting will be held only if the customer requests said hearing.
   B.   A deferred payment plan is hereby adopted by the Town Board of Trustees
and is only available for those customers with documentation from a treating
physician stating that no utility service to said customer's residence may
result in life threatening or endangering circumstances to one (1) or more
occupants of the residence.
   C.   Upon termination of service, a notice of termination shall be left at
each residence where service is terminated. Said notice of termination shall
state that service has been terminated, balance due, including all additional
charges, procedure for arranging a deferred payment plan, the customer meets
the criteria for a deferred payment plan as previously stated in this section,
and procedure for reconnection. (2011 Code § 19-112A)
9-2B-3: DISHONORED CHECKS:
   A.   In the event any customer should offer payment for any monthly bill, or
portion thereof, by means of a check which is not honored on account of
insufficient funds of the maker to pay same, or because the check is drawn on a
closed account or on a nonexistent account, or otherwise dishonored, a check
service charge in the amount set and established by resolution of the Board of
Trustees of the Mooreland Public Works Authority and approved and adopted by
resolution of the Town Board of Trustees, and posted for inspection in the
Office of the Town Clerk- Treasurer shall be charged and collected as a service
charge for proper handling and administration. (2011 Code § 9-113; amd. 2017
Code)
   B.   Failure to replace the dishonored check with cash or certified/
cashier's check before three o'clock (3:00) P.M. on the next working day after
notification by posting of note on the door of the address from which the check
has been returned will result in immediate disconnection of utility service.
   C.   In the event that two (2) such dishonored checks are made to the Town
for utility service within any last preceding twelve (12) month period, payment
of each monthly bill by such customer/consumer for the next twelve (12) month
period of ensuing service shall be made and accepted only when tendered by
certified or cashier's check or cash. (2011 Code § 19-113)
9-2B-4: PAYMENT EXTENSIONS:
   A.   Two (2) extensions per calendar year may be granted upon the request of
the consumer; provided, that the utility payment extension agreement is
completed and approved by the Town Clerk- Treasurer or Town Administrator prior
to notification at the residence that services will be cut off. All extensions
will be extended to the last working day of the month the bill is currently
due.
   B.   Failure to comply with any extension agreement will result in
disconnection of service without further notice, and no additional extension
will be granted for one (1) year from the date of the broken agreement. (2011
Code § 19-114)
9-2B-5: SUMMARY OF POLICIES AFTER POSTED NOTICE:
   A.   Business And Residential Cutoff:
      1.   Weather does not affect cutoff.
      2.   Payments of all past due amounts made before one o'clock (1:00) P.M.
of the day indicated for cutoff will stop cutoff.
      3.   Bad checks are to be picked up with cash by three o'clock (3:00)
P.M. the first business day after contact is made.
      4.   Once service has been disconnected, payment of the entire balance on
the account is required, together with the appropriate service call charge,
before service will be resumed. (2011 Code § 19-115)
      5.   When service is reconnected during normal working hours, a service
call charge set and established by resolution of the Board of Trustees of the
Mooreland Public Works Authority and approved and adopted by resolution of the
Town Board of Trustees, and posted for inspection in the Office of the Town
Clerk- Treasurer will be made. A charge set and established by resolution of
the Board of Trustees of the Mooreland Public Works Authority and approved and
adopted by resolution of the Town Board of Trustees, and posted for inspection
