in the Office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer will be made for reconnections made
after normal working hours. (2011 Code § 19-115; amd. 2017 Code)
      6.   Cutoff and standby employees will be instructed to inform the
consumer of immediate need to make contact with Town Hall to delay
disconnection procedures. Disconnection will proceed if the employee can
determine such contact has not been made.
   B.   Extension For Payment: Any extension of time for payment must be
approved by the Town Clerk-Treasurer or Town Administrator. (2011 Code § 19-
115)
9-2B-6: SUMMARY OF COLLECTION POLICIES:
In the event any customer should fail to make payment on any monthly billing so
that said bill is over fifty (50) days in arrears, the Town's Utility
Superintendent shall notify the customer/consumer at the address shown on the
Town records that the customer shall, within five (5) working days, contact the
Town Clerk-Treasurer to make satisfaction of said bill under the terms and
conditions of section
9-2B-5 of this article. Should the customer/consumer fail to comply with
section
9-2B-5 of this article, the Town's Utility Superintendent shall be directed at
his earliest opportunity to refer said customer's bill for legal collection
procedures. (2011 Code § 19-116)
ARTICLE C. FRAUDULENT USE OF SERVICES
SECTION:
9-2C-1: Definition
9-2C-2: Fraudulent Use Of Services
9-2C-3: Tampering With Utility Equipment Or Property
9-2C-1: DEFINITION:
For the purpose of this article, the term "fraudulent use of service" shall
include any unauthorized use of the Town's electric, sewer, water and garbage
services and facilities by the consumer. (2011 Code § 19-117; amd. 2017 Code)
9-2C-2: FRAUDULENT USE OF SERVICES:
In the event fraudulent use of a service or evidence of attempted fraudulent
use of a service is discovered, or where the Town's regulating or measuring
equipment or other property has been tampered with, service(s) may be
disconnected by the Town without advance notice to the consumer. Service to the
consumer will not be resumed until the consumer shall have paid all bills
including:
   A.   The charge for the estimated amount of service fraudulently consumed.
   B.   The cost of replacement or repair of any damaged meter or associated
equipment. (2011 Code § 19-117)
   C.   A reconnection charge set and established by resolution of the Board of
Trustees of the Mooreland Public Works Authority and approved and adopted by
resolution of the Town Board of Trustees, and posted for inspection in the
Office of the Town Clerk- Treasurer. (2011 Code § 19-117; amd. 2017 Code)
   D.   If service has been restored by other than Town personnel after having
been disconnected initially for one (1) of the reasons stated herein, the
consumer shall, in addition to the charges enumerated above, pay a charge set
and established by the Board of Trustees of the Mooreland Public Works
Authority and approved and adopted by the Town Board of Trustees, and posted
for inspection in the Office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer.
   E.   If it has been shown to the satisfaction of the Town that the consumer
or applicant for service had no connection with or knowledge of such fraudulent
use of service(s) or such tampering, service may be resumed after the condition
causing or permitting the fraudulent usage has been corrected and such consumer
or applicant for service has paid for any unmetered service received. (2011
Code § 19-117)
9-2C-3: TAMPERING WITH UTILITY EQUIPMENT OR PROPERTY:
No regulating or measuring equipment or other property or equipment owned by
the Town, wherever situated, whether upon the consumer's premises or elsewhere,
shall be tampered with or interfered with for the purpose of adjustment,
fraudulent adjustment or otherwise. In the event equipment has been tampered
with, the Town will follow the same procedures as for fraudulent use of
services as outlined in section
9-2C-2 of this article. (2011 Code § 19-118)
CHAPTER 3
ELECTRIC SERVICE
SECTION:
9-3-1: Definitions
9-3-2: Rates And Deposits
9-3-3: Cost Adjustments
9-3-4: Meters
9-3-1: DEFINITIONS:
When used in this chapter, the following words and terms shall have the
meanings ascribed to them in this section:
DEPARTMENT: The Electric Light Department of the Town of Mooreland, and any act
in this chapter required to be done by the Town of Mooreland, hereinafter
called the "Town", shall be done on its behalf by an authorized employee of the
Electric Light Department.
PERSON: Natural persons of either sex, any association, copartnership, express
trust, or corporation, whether acting by themselves or by a servant, agent, or
employee; the singular person shall be held and construed to include the
plural, and the masculine pronoun to include the feminine. (2011 Code § 19-1)
9-3-2: RATES AND DEPOSITS:
   A.   Rates: The Town shall charge rates for electricity set and established
by resolution of the Board of Trustees of the Mooreland Public Works Authority
and approved and adopted by resolution of the Town Board of Trustees, and
posted for inspection in the Office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer. (2011 Code §
19-2; amd. 2017 Code)
   B.   Deposits: For electric service to be established for any customer, a
security deposit shall be required in the following amounts: (2017 Code)
      1.   Owner: One hundred fifty dollars ($150.00).
      2.   Renter: One hundred seventy five dollars ($175.00). (Ord. 310, 8-11-
2014)
9-3-3: COST ADJUSTMENTS:
Fuel costs dictate the price at which electricity may be obtained by the Town.
When said fuel costs increase, it makes necessary an increase in the rates for
electricity which must be charged to citizens receiving electricity through the
Town. As stated in subs
9-3-2A of this chapter, the Board of Trustees of the Mooreland Public Works
Authority may adopt power cost adjustments as dictated by fuel cost increases.
When such occurs, the rates and schedules shall be amended and posted pursuant
to subs
9-3-2A of this chapter. The current adjustment shall be as adopted by ordinance
250 as if set out in full herein. (2011 Code § 19-3)
9-3-4: METERS:
   A.   Property Of Town: All meters put in by the Town shall be and remain the
property of the Town and will not be removed unless the use of the electricity
on the premises is to be entirely stopped or the service connections
discontinued. (2011 Code § 19-4)
   B.   Lost, Damaged Meter: In all cases where meters are lost, injured, or
broken by carelessness or negligence of the owner or occupant of the premises,
they shall be replaced or repaired by or under the direction of Town agent(s)
and the cost charged against the owner or occupant. (2011 Code § 19-4; amd.
2017 Code)
   C.   Inaccurate Meter; Testing:
      1.   In the event the meter may be getting out of order or failing to
register properly, the consumer shall be charged on an estimate made by the
Town Clerk-Treasurer and/or the Town Administrator on the average monthly
consumption during the last three (3) months that the same was in good order,
or for what he may consider to be the most reliable data at his command. (2011
Code § 19-4)
      2.   If a parallel meter is required for the testing of the accuracy of a
meter, at the consumer's request, a fee set and established by resolution of
the Board of Trustees of the Mooreland Public Works Authority and approved and
adopted by resolution of the Town Board of Trustees, and posted for inspection
in the Office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer shall be assessed. The fee will be
waived if it is determined that there is a problem with the current meter.
   D.   Inaccessible Meter: If access to any occupant's meter is denied for
whatever reason in order to obtain the monthly reading resulting in the Town
having to call the occupant for the reading, the occupant will be charged a fee
set and established by resolution of the Board of Trustees of the Mooreland
Public Works Authority and approved and adopted by resolution of the Town Board
of Trustees, and posted for inspection in the Office of the Town Clerk-
Treasurer, which will be included on the occupant's monthly statement. (2011
Code § 19-4; amd. 2017 Code)
CHAPTER 4
WATER SERVICE
SECTION:
9-4-1: System A Public Utility
9-4-2: Superintendent
9-4-3: Tapping Charges
9-4-4: Connection To System
9-4-5: Meters
9-4-6: Service To More Than One Premises By A Single Connection
9-4-7: Rates And Deposits
9-4-8: Conservation Measures
9-4-9: Interference With, Obstruction Of, Damage To System
9-4-10: Entry Powers For Inspections
9-4-1: SYSTEM A PUBLIC UTILITY:
The water and water distribution system of the Town is hereby declared to be a
public utility and a proper source of revenue for Municipal purposes. (2011
Code § 19-10)
9-4-2: SUPERINTENDENT:
The word "Superintendent", wherever used in this chapter, shall be held to mean
the Superintendent or foreman of the Town Water Department. When any act is
required to be done by him, the same may be done on behalf of the
Superintendent by any authorized officer or employee of the Water Department.
All such superintendents and employees shall be at all times under the direct
supervision and subject to the orders and control of the Mayor and Board of
Trustees. (2011 Code § 19-12)
9-4-3: TAPPING CHARGES:
   A.   The Town shall charge rates for the tapping of water lines by the Town,
including the installation of a meter, meter box, fittings, and service line to
the property line, but generally not to exceed forty feet (40') thereof
according to the schedules determined by the Town Board. (2011 Code § 19-11)
   B.   Said rates and schedules shall be set and established by resolution of
the Board of Trustees of the Mooreland Public Works Authority and approved and
adopted by resolution of the Town Board of Trustees, and posted for inspection
in the Office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer. (2011 Code § 19-11; amd. 2017 Code)
   C.   Such charges shall be paid to the Town Clerk-Treasurer prior to the
installation of such equipment and/or service. (2011 Code § 19-11)
9-4-4: CONNECTION TO SYSTEM:
   A.   Connection Required:
      1.   Each occupied residence and each occupied business or commercial
building in the Town shall connect to the Town's water system within sixty (60)
days after the effective date hereof; provided, however, that such service
shall be brought within at least one hundred fifty feet (150') of the residence
or business property line. (2011 Code § 19-22)
      2.   Any person, firm, corporation or entity violating any provision of
this subsection A shall, upon conviction thereof, be punishable as provided in
section
1-4-1 of this Code, and each day that any violation of any provision of this
subsection is allowed to exist shall be and constitute a separate offense.
(2011 Code § 19-22; amd. 2017 Code)
   B.   Owner Or Occupant Request For Service: Whenever the owner or occupant
of any premises connecting with the Town water supply system shall desire to
use the water, he shall notify the Superintendent and request that the water be
turned on to the premises. The owner shall leave his portion of the service
exposed in the trench until water is turned on by the Superintendent, when the
owner shall immediately properly cover the pipe. (2011 Code § 19-13)
9-4-5: METERS:
   A.   Property Of Town: All meters put in by the Town shall be and remain the
property of the Town and will not be removed unless the use of the water on the
premises is to be entirely stopped or the service connections discontinued.
   B.   Lost, Damaged Meter: In all cases where meters are lost, injured, or
broken by carelessness or negligence of the owner or occupant of the premises,
they shall be replaced or repaired by or under the direction of the
Superintendent and the cost charged against the owner or occupant.
   C.   Inaccurate Meter; Testing:
      1.   In the event the meter may be getting out of order or failing to
register properly, the consumer shall be charged on an estimate made by the
Superintendent on the average monthly consumption during the last three (3)
months that the same was in good order, or for what he may consider to be the
most reliable data at his command. (2011 Code § 19-15)
      2.   Where accuracy of record of the water meter is questioned, it shall
be removed at the customer's request, and shall, in his presence, be tested in
the shops of the Water Department by means of the apparatus there provided, and
a report thereon duly made. Both parties to the test must accept the finding so
made. If the test discloses an error against the consumer of more than three
percent (3%) in the meter's registry, the excess of the consumption on the
three (3) previous readings shall be credited to the customer's account, and
the Water Department shall bear the entire expense of the test and the deposit
set out in subs
9-4-7B of this chapter shall be returned. On the other hand, where no such
error is found, the person who has requested the test shall pay the actual cost
for such test including costs incurred by the Town due to wages of employees
involved.
      3.   No meter shall be removed or in any way be disturbed, or seal
broken, except in the presence of and under the direction of the
Superintendent. (2011 Code § 19-16)
   D.   Inaccessible Meter: If access to any occupant's meter is denied for
whatever reason in order to obtain the monthly reading resulting in the Town
having to call the occupant for the reading, the occupant will be charged a fee
set and established by resolution of the Board of Trustees of the Mooreland
Public Works Authority and approved and adopted by resolution of the Town Board
of Trustees, and posted for inspection in the Office of the Town Clerk-
Treasurer, which will be included on the occupant's monthly statement. (2011
Code § 19-15; amd. 2017 Code)
9-4-6: SERVICE TO MORE THAN ONE PREMISES BY A SINGLE CONNECTION:
When several houses, buildings, or premises are supplied or are to be supplied
with water through one (1) service connection with the Town main, the
Superintendent may, in his discretion, either decline to furnish water until
separate services are provided or the service metered, or in case any one (1)
of the owners or occupants becomes delinquent or violates any of the provisions
of this chapter, the Superintendent may shut off the original or main service
until all delinquent and unpaid charges and other charges are paid, and the
premises supplied by the main service shall be held responsible for all
delinquent and unpaid charges against any one (1) or all of the separate owners
or users. No change of ownership or occupation shall affect the application of
this section. (2011 Code § 19-19)
9-4-7: RATES AND DEPOSITS:
   A.   Rates:
      1.   Established: The water rates charged to consumers of water from the
water system of the Town are set and established by resolution of the Board of
Trustees of the Mooreland Public Works Authority and approved and adopted by
resolution of the Town Board of Trustees, and posted for inspection in the
Office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer. (Ord. 329, 3-13-2017; amd. 2017 Code)
      2.   Annual Fee Adjustment: Commencing July 1, 2017, and continuing each
subsequent July 1, the Board of Trustees shall review the fees charged and
shall recommend adjustment of the fees to the Town Board based upon the
percentage change in the consumer price index, all urban consumers, south
region, all items, during the twelve (12) month period ending in April
preceding the July in question. Any recommended change shall be rounded up to
the nearest nickel. (Ord. 329, 3-13-2017)
   B.   Deposits:
      1.   For water service to be established for any customer, a security
deposit shall be required in the following amounts:
         a.   Property owners: Fifty dollars ($50.00).
         b.   Property renters: Seventy five dollars ($75.00).
      2.   Deposits shall be refunded to customers upon full and final payment
of accounts due and may be applied to the balance of accounts if the customer
exceeds time requirements for said final payment. (Ord. 311, 8-11-2014)
9-4-8: CONSERVATION MEASURES:
The use of water for sprinkling or irrigating lawns, gardens, flowerbeds,
plants, trees, shrubs, parking strips, or hosing windows, woodwork, porches,
steps, or walks may be prohibited by the Water Superintendent, Mayor or Town
Board of Trustees during such periods as may be deemed necessary to conserve
the supply of water; and shall become effective upon notice thereof being given
by publication in a newspaper of general circulation in the Town, or by other
methods as determined by the Town Board of Trustees. (2011 Code § 19-14; amd.
2017 Code)
9-4-9: INTERFERENCE WITH, OBSTRUCTION OF, DAMAGE TO SYSTEM:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any person, except one duly authorized by the
Superintendent or a member of the Fire Department, or by a person authorized by
the Mayor, to open, operate, close, turn off, interfere with, attach any pipe
or hose to, or connect with any fire hydrant, stop valve, or stopcock belonging
to the Town. (2011 Code § 19-17)
   B.   It shall be unlawful for any person to obstruct the access to any fire
hydrant or place around or thereon any stone, brick, lumber, or dirt, or
wilfully or negligently injure the same. (2011 Code § 19-18)
   C.   It shall be unlawful for any person, unless duly authorized by the
Superintendent, to disturb, interfere with or damage any water main, water
pipe, machinery, tools, buildings, improvements, lawns, grass plots, flowers,
vines, bushes, or trees belonging to, connected with, or under the control of
the water system of the Town. (2011 Code § 19-21)
9-4-10: ENTRY POWERS FOR INSPECTIONS:
Any officer, inspector, foreman, or authorized employee of the department shall
have free access at all reasonable hours to any premises supplied with Town
water for the purpose of making any inspection of the water supply upon said
premises. In case any authorized employee is refused admittance to any premises
or, being admitted, shall be hindered or prevented in making such examination,
the Superintendent may cause the water to be turned off from said premises.
(2011 Code § 19-20)
CHAPTER 5
SEWER SERVICE
SECTION:
9-5-1: System A Public Utility
9-5-2: Definitions
9-5-3: Use Of Public Sewers Required; Tapping Charges
9-5-4: Private Sewage Disposal Systems
9-5-5: Building Sewers And Connections
9-5-6: Use Of The Sanitary Sewer System
9-5-6-1: Discharges Into System
9-5-6-2: Interceptors
9-5-6-3: Preliminary Treatment Or Flow Equalization
9-5-6-4: Control Manhole
9-5-6-5: Measurements, Tests And Analyses
9-5-6-6: Special Agreements
9-5-7: User Charges; Industrial Users
9-5-8: Users Outside Town Limits
9-5-9: Tampering With, Damaging System
9-5-10: Powers And Authority Of Inspectors
9-5-11: Violations; Penalties
9-5-1: SYSTEM A PUBLIC UTILITY:
The sanitary sewerage system of the Town is hereby declared to be a public
utility and a proper source of revenue for the upkeep and maintenance of the
system and for other purposes. (2011 Code § 19-31)
9-5-2: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this chapter, certain terms and words are to be used and
interpreted as defined in this section:
BOD (BIOCHEMICAL OXYGEN DEMAND): The quantity of oxygen utilized in the
biochemical oxidation of organic matter under standard laboratory procedure in
five (5) days at twenty degrees Celsius (20°C), expressed in milligrams per
liter.
BUILDING DRAIN: That part of the lowest horizontal piping of a drainage system
which receives the discharge from soil, waste and other drainage pipes inside
the walls of the building and conveys it to the building sewer, beginning five
feet (5') (1.5 m) outside the inner face of the building wall.
BUILDING SEWER: The extension from the building drain to the public sewer or
other place of disposal.
COMBINED SEWER: A sewer receiving both surface runoff and sewage.
CUSTOMER: The owner of the property served by a water connection, or the
tenant, lessee, renter, establishment, institution, or occupant of such
property, or the person in or against whose name the water connection for such
property is listed on the books and records of the Town of Mooreland, Oklahoma,
and who is responsible to the Town for the payment of bills incurred for water
furnished to the property, and for use by such property of the sanitary sewage
system of the Town, either or both.
DOMESTIC WASTEWATER: The liquid wastes: a) from the noncommercial preparation,
cooking, and handling of food; or b) containing human excrement and similar
matter from the sanitary conveniences of dwellings, commercial buildings,
industrial facilities and institutions.
GARBAGE: Solid wastes from the domestic and commercial preparation, cooking,
and dispensing of food, and from the handling, storage and sale of produce.
ICR (INDUSTRIAL COST RECOVERY CHARGE): Recovery by the Town from the industrial
users of the treatment works of the Federal grant amount allocable to the
treatment of sewage from such users, pursuant to section 204(b) of Public Law
92-500 and the applicable rules and regulations.
INDUSTRIAL SEWAGE: The liquid waste resulting from any process of industry,
manufacturing, trade or business including cooling water that is discharged to
the sanitary sewerage system.
INDUSTRIAL USER:
   A.   Any nongovernmental user of publicly owned treatment works identified
in the Standard Industrial Classification Manual, Office of Management and
Budget, as amended and supplemented under the following divisions:
      1. Division A, agriculture, forestry, and fishing.
      2. Division B, mining.
      3. Division D, manufacturing.
      4. Division E, transportation, communications, electric, gas and sanitary
services.
      5. Division I, services.
   B.   A user in the divisions listed may be excluded if it is determined that
it will introduce primarily segregated domestic wastes or wastes from sanitary
conveniences.
   C.   Any industrial user who discharges one thousand forty two (1,042)
gallons per hour (GP) (25,000 gallons per day) or less of domestic wastewater
or whose combined process and domestic wastewater is equivalent to one thousand
forty two (1,042) GP or less of domestic water is exempted from the industrial
cost recovery charge, provided his discharge does not contain pollutants which
interfere, or are incompatible with, or contaminate or reduce the utility of
the sludge from the Municipal wastewater treatment plant.
mg/l: Milligrams per liter.
NATURAL OUTLET: Any outlet into a watercourse, pond, ditch, lake or other body
of surface water or groundwater.
NORMAL STRENGTH SEWAGE: Sewage discharged by a user into the sanitary sewers
and in which the average concentrations of total suspended solids (SS) is not
more than three hundred milligrams per liter (300 mg/l) and biochemical oxygen
demand (BOD) is not more than three hundred milligrams per liter (300 mg/l).
PERSON: Any individual, firm, company, association, society, corporation or
group.
ph: The logarithm of the reciprocal of the weight of hydrogen ions in grams per
liter of solution.
PLUMBING INSPECTOR: That person designated by the Town Board to inspect work
and compliance with this Code, ordinances and laws governing the installation
and operation of sewer, water and gas plumbing.
PROPERLY SHREDDED GARBAGE: The wastes from the preparation, cooking and
dispensing of food that have been shredded to such a degree that all particles
will be carried freely under the flow conditions normally prevailing in public
sewers, with no particle greater than one-half inch (1/2") (1.27 cm) in any
dimension.
PUBLIC SEWER: A sewer in which all owners of abutting properties have equal
rights and is controlled by the Public Authority.
SANITARY SEWAGE: The "domestic wastewater" as defined in this section.
SANITARY SEWER: A sewer which carries sewage and to which stormwater, surface
water and groundwater are not intentionally admitted.
SANITARY SEWERAGE SYSTEM: All sanitary sewer trunk lines, main lines, submain
lines, lateral lines, lift stations and sewage treatment plants, and all sewer
lines connected to the Town's sewer lines or treatment plants, whether owned by
the Town or not.
SEWAGE: A combination of the water carried wastes from residents, business
buildings, institutions and industrial establishments, together with such
groundwater, surface water and stormwater as may be present and includes the
domestic wastewater and industrial sewage in any combination.
SEWAGE TREATMENT PLANT: Any arrangement of devices and structures used for
treating sewage.
SEWAGE WORKS: All facilities for collecting, pumping, treating and disposing of
sewage.
SEWER SERVICE RATE: The price per unit (mg/l, 1,000 gallons, pounds, etc.) of
waste discharged into the sanitary sewerage system of the Town of Mooreland,
Oklahoma.
SHALL; MAY: "Shall" is mandatory; "may" is permissive.
SLUG: Any discharge of water, sewage or industrial waste, which concentration
of any given constituent or in quantity of flow exceeds for any period of
duration longer than fifteen (15) minutes more than five (5) times the average
twenty four (24) hour concentration of flows during normal operation.
STORM DRAIN (Sometimes Read STORM SEWER): A sewer which carries stormwater,
surface water and drainage, but excludes sewerage and industrial wastes, other
than unpolluted cooling water.
SUSPENDED SOLIDS: Solids that either float on the surface of or are in
suspension in water, sewage or other liquids, and which are removable by
laboratory filtering.
TOWN AGENT: The Town agent of sewage works and/or of water pollution control of
the Town of Mooreland, Oklahoma, or his authorized deputy, agent or
representative.
USER: A "customer", as defined in this section, whose property also discharges
sewage into the sanitary sewerage system of the Town of Mooreland, Oklahoma, in
any quantity.
USER CHARGE: The monthly charge fixed for the user based upon the volume and
strength of sewage determined to be discharged by the user into the sanitary
sewerage system of the Town.
WATERCOURSE: A channel in which a flow of water occurs, either continuously or
intermittently. (2011 Code § 19-34; amd. 2017 Code)
9-5-3: USE OF PUBLIC SEWERS REQUIRED; TAPPING CHARGES:
   A.   Discharge Of Objectionable Wastes: It shall be unlawful for any person
to place, deposit or permit to be deposited in any unsanitary manner on public
or private property within the Town, or in any area under the jurisdiction of
the Town, any human or animal excrement, garbage or other objectionable waste.
(2011 Code § 19-35)
   B.   Treatment Required: It shall be unlawful to discharge to any natural
outlet within the Town, or in any area under the jurisdiction of the Town, any
sewage or other polluted waters except where suitable treatment has been
provided in accordance with the provisions of this chapter. (2011 Code § 19-36)
   C.   Private Systems: Except as hereinafter provided, it shall be unlawful
to construct or maintain any privy, privy vault, septic tank, cesspool or other
facility intended or used for the disposal of sewage. (2011 Code § 19-37)
   D.   Connection To Sewer System Required: The owner of all houses, buildings
or properties used for human occupancy, employment, recreation or other
purposes situated within the Town and abutting on any street, alley or right-
of-way in which there is now located or may in the future be located a public
sanitary or combined sewer of the Town is hereby required, at his expense, to
install suitable toilet facilities thereon, and to connect such facilities
directly with the proper public sewer in accordance with the provisions of this
chapter within ninety (90) days after date of official notice to do so;
provided, that said public sewer is within five hundred feet (500') of the
property line. (2011 Code § 19-38; amd. 2017 Code)
   E.   Tapping Charges:
      1.   The Town shall charge rates for the tapping of and the tying into
the sanitary sewer system in the Town and all that portion of the Town
hereinafter brought within the corporate limits of the Town according to the
schedule set and established by resolution of the Board of Trustees of the
Mooreland Public Works Authority and approved and adopted by resolution of the
Town Board of Trustees, and posted for inspection in the Office of the Town
Clerk-Treasurer.
      2.   The amount of such charges, rates, and schedules, and the amount of
line to be furnished, normally not to exceed forty feet (40') of four inch (4")
service line to the property line, shall be set and established by resolution
of the Board of Trustees of the Mooreland Public Works Authority and approved
and adopted by resolution of the Town Board of Trustees, and posted for
inspection in the Office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer.
      3.   Such charges established by subsection E2 of this section shall be
paid to the Clerk-Treasurer prior to installation of such equipment and/or
service. (2011 Code § 19-32; amd. 2017 Code)
9-5-4: PRIVATE SEWAGE DISPOSAL SYSTEMS:
   A.   Private Systems Permitted: Where a public sanitary or combined sewer is
not available under the provisions of subs
9-5-3D of this chapter, the building sewer shall be connected to a private
sewage disposal system complying with the provisions of this section. (2011
Code § 19-39)
   B.   Permit Requirements:
      1.   Before commencement of construction of a private sewage disposal
system, the owner shall first obtain a written permit signed by the County
Health Department. The application for such permit shall be made on a form
furnished by the Health Department which the applicant shall supplement by any
plans, specifications and other information as is deemed necessary by the
Health Department. (2011 Code § 19-40)
      2.   A permit for a private sewage disposal system shall not become
effective until the installation is completed to the satisfaction of the County
Health Department. Representatives shall be allowed to inspect the work at any
stage of construction, and in any event, the applicant for the permit shall
notify the Health Department when the work is ready for final inspection and
before any underground portions are covered. (2011 Code § 19-41)
   C.   Specifications: The type, capacities, location and layout of a private
sewage disposal system shall comply with all recommendations of the Department
of Public Health of the State of Oklahoma. No septic tank or cesspool shall be
permitted to discharge to any natural outlet. (2011 Code § 19-42)
   D.   Maintenance: The owner shall operate and maintain the private sewage
disposal facilities in a sanitary manner at all times at no expense to the
Town. (2011 Code § 19-44)
   E.   Availability Of Public Sewer; Connection Required: At such time as a
public sewer becomes available to a property served by a private disposal
system, as provided in subs
9-5-3D of this chapter, a direct connection shall be made to the public sewer
in compliance with this chapter, and any septic tanks, cesspools and similar
private sewage disposal facilities shall be abandoned and filled with suitable
material. (2011 Code § 19-43)
   F.   Additional Requirements: No statement contained in this section shall
be construed to interfere with any additional requirements that may be imposed
by the Health Officer. (2011 Code § 19-45)
9-5-5: BUILDING SEWERS AND CONNECTIONS:
   A.   Permit To Connect:
      1.   Permit Required: No unauthorized person shall uncover, make any
connections with or opening into, use, alter or disturb any public sewer or
appurtenance thereof without first obtaining a written permit from the plumbing
inspector. (2011 Code § 19-47)
      2.   Classes Of Permits: There shall be two (2) classes of building sewer
permits: a) for residential and commercial service; and b) for service to
establishments producing industrial wastes. In either case, the owner or his
agent shall make application on a special form furnished by the Town. The
permit application shall be supplemented by any plans, specifications or other
information considered pertinent in the judgment of the plumbing inspector.
(2011 Code § 19-48)
      3.   Permit And Inspection Fee: A permit and inspection fee set and
established by resolution of the Board of Trustees of the Mooreland Public
Works Authority and approved and adopted by resolution of the Town Board of
Trustees, and posted for inspection in the Office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer
for a residential, commercial or industrial building sewer permit shall be paid
to the Town at the time the application is filed. (2011 Code § 19-48; amd. 2017
Code)
   B.   Separate Building Sewers Required; Exception: A separate and
independent building sewer shall be provided for every building; except, where
one (1) building stands at the rear of another on an interior lot and no
private sewer is available or can be constructed to the rear building through
an adjoining alley, court, yard or driveway, the building sewer from the front
building may be extended to the rear building and the whole considered as one
(1) building sewer. (2011 Code § 19-50)
   C.   Use Of Existing Building Sewers: Old building sewers may be used in
connection with new buildings only when they are found, on examination and
tests by the plumbing inspector, to meet all requirements of this chapter.
(2011 Code § 19-51)
   D.   Installation And Construction Requirements And Specifications:
      1.   The size, slope, alignment, and materials of construction of a
sewer, and the methods to be used in excavating, placing of the pipe, jointing,
testing and backfilling the trench, shall all conform to the requirements of
the Building and Plumbing Codes or other applicable rules and regulations of
the Town. In the absence of Code provisions or in amplification thereof, the
materials and procedures set forth in appropriate specifications of the ASTM
and WPCF Manual of Practice No. 9 shall apply. (2011 Code § 19-52)
      2.   Whenever possible, the building sewer shall be brought to the
building at an elevation below the basement floor. In all buildings in which
any building drain is too low to permit gravity flow to the public sewer,
sanitary sewage carried by such building drain shall be lifted by an approved
means and discharged. (2011 Code § 19-53)
      3.   All connections shall be made gastight and watertight. Any deviation
from the prescribed procedures and materials must be approved by the plumbing
inspector before installation. (2011 Code § 19-55)
      4.   All excavations for building sewer installation shall be adequately
guarded with barricades and lights so as to protect the public from hazard.
Streets, sidewalks, parkways and other public property disturbed in the course
of the work shall be restored in a manner satisfactory to the Town. (2011 Code
§ 19-57)
   E.   Discharge Of Stormwater Or Surface Waters Prohibited: No person shall
make any connection of roof downspouts, exterior foundation drains, areaway
drains or other sources of surface runoff or groundwater to a building sewer or
building drain which in turn is connected directly or indirectly to a public
sanitary sewer. (2011 Code § 19-54)
   F.   Inspections: The applicant for the building sewer permit shall notify
the plumbing inspector when the building sewer is ready for inspection and
connection to the public sewer. The connection shall be made under the
supervision of the plumbing inspector or his representative. (2011 Code § 19-
56)
   G.   Liability For Costs And Expenses: All costs and expenses incident to
the installation and connection of the building sewer shall be borne by the
owner. The owner shall indemnify the Town from any loss or damage that may
directly or indirectly be occasioned by the installation of the building sewer.
(2011 Code § 19-49)
9-5-6: USE OF THE SANITARY SEWER SYSTEM:
9-5-6-1: DISCHARGES INTO SYSTEM:
   A.   Stormwater And Surface Waters:
      1.   No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any stormwater,
surface water, groundwater, roof runoff, subsurface drainage, uncontaminated
cooling water, or unpolluted industrial process waters to any sanitary sewer.
(2011 Code § 19-48)
      2.   Stormwater and all other unpolluted drainage shall be discharged to
such sewers as are specifically designated as combined sewers or storm sewers,
or to a natural outlet approved by the Town agent. Industrial cooling water or
unpolluted process waters may be discharged, on approval of the Town agent, to
a storm sewer, combined sewer or natural outlet. (2011 Code § 19-59; amd. 2017
Code)
   B.   Prohibited And Restricted Discharges:
      1.   No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any of the
following described waters or wastes to any public sewers:
         a.   Any gasoline, benzene, naphtha, fuel oil or other flammable or
explosive liquid, solid or gas.
         b.   Any waters or wastes containing toxic or poisonous solids,
liquids or gases in sufficient quantity, either singly or by interaction with
other wastes, to injure or interfere with any sewage treatment process or
facility, constitute a hazard to humans or animals, create a public nuisance or
create any hazard in the receiving waters of sewage treatment plant effluent.
         c.   Any waters or wastes having a pH lower than 5.5, or causing the
pH of the sewage plant influent to rise above 9.5, or having any other
corrosive property capable of causing damage or hazard to processes,
structures, equipment and/or personnel of the sewage works.
         d.   Solid, viscous or liquid substances in quantities or of such size
as to cause or be capable of causing obstruction to the flow in sewers or other
interference with the proper operation of the sewage works such as, but not
limited to, ashes; cinders; sand; mud; straw; shavings; metal; glass; rags;
feathers; tar; plastics; wood; unground garbage; whole blood; paunch manure;
hair and fleshing; entrails; paper products such as dishes, cups, milk
containers, etc., either whole or ground by garbage grinders; slops; chemical
residues; or bulk solids.
         e.   Any strong acid, iron pickling wastes or concentrated plating
solutions, whether neutralized or not.
         f.   Any unusual volume of flow or concentration of wastes
constituting "slugs" as defined in section
9-5-2 of this chapter.
         g.   Any substance that may pass through the treatment plant without
being effectively treated or otherwise reduced to acceptable concentrations by
normal treatment methods such that the sewage treatment plant effluent cannot
meet the requirements of other agencies having jurisdiction over the discharge
to the receiving waters.
         h.   Any waste containing rheum, strontium, or tellurium.
         i.   Any waters or wastes containing substances in excess of the
limits established in subsection B2 of this section or that have been diluted
solely for the purpose of meeting any concentration limits listed or implied in
this subsection.
      2.   No person shall discharge or cause to be discharged any of the
following described substances, materials, waters, or wastes in concentrations,
quantities or rates in excess of those listed except as hereinafter provided:
         a.   Any liquid or vapor having a temperature higher than one hundred
fifty degrees Fahrenheit (150°F) (65°C), or any substance which causes the
temperature of the total sewage plant influent to increase at a rate of ten
degrees Fahrenheit (10°F) or more per hour or a combined total increase of
plant influent temperature to one hundred ten degrees Fahrenheit (110°F).
         b.   Any water or waste containing fats, wax, grease or oil, whether
emulsified or not, in excess of one hundred milligrams per liter (100 mg/l) or
containing substances which may solidify or become viscous at temperatures
between thirty two degrees (32°) and one hundred fifty degrees Fahrenheit
(150°F) (0 and 65°C). (2011 Code § 19-65)
         c.   Any garbage that has not been properly shredded. The installation
and operation of any garbage shredder equipped with a motor of three-fourths
(3/4) horsepower (0.76 hp metric) or greater shall be subject to review and
approval of the Town agent.
         d.   Any radioactive wastes or isotopes of such half-life or
concentration as may exceed limits to be established by the Town agent on a
case by case basis in compliance with and after consultation with the
appropriate regulatory agencies.
         e.   Any substance with a BOD or suspended solids concentration in
excess of three hundred milligrams per liter (300 mg/l); except, that upon
receipt of a written application and establishment of appropriate charges, the
Town agent may, if the sewage works has sufficient unused or uncommitted
capacity, authorize the discharge of wastes containing BOD and/or suspended
solids concentrations in excess of three hundred milligrams per liter (300 mg/
l) each. (2011 Code § 19-65; amd. 2017 Code)
         f.   Any waters or wastes with total dissolved solids concentrations
greater than three thousand milligrams per liter (3,000 mg/l), plus the
dissolved solids in the Town water supply.
         g.   Any waters or wastes containing excessive discoloration or
causing excess discoloration of the effluent including, but not limited to, dye
wastes and vegetable tanning solutions.
         h.   Any waters, wastes or other substances containing one (1) or more
of the following constituents in excess of the concentrations listed:
 Average For 30 Consecutive Days (mg/l) Maximum For Any 1 Day (mg/l)
                    Average For 30 Consecutive Maximum For Any 1 Day (mg/l)
                    Days (mg/l)
Antimony            0.01
Arsenic             0.1
Boron               1.0
Cadmium             0.5                        1.0
Chromium-hexavalent 1.0
Chromium-total      5.0
Copper              1.0

Mercury             0.002
Nickel              1.8                        3.6
Phenols             0.1
Silver              0.3                        1.0
Vanadium            10.0
Zinc                5.0
 
      3.   Limitation on elements or compounds not listed will be established
and/or limitations for elements or compounds listed will be lowered if
necessary to ensure that the effluent of the wastewater treatment plant is in
full compliance with legal requirements of County, State or Federal regulatory
agencies. (2011 Code § 19-65)
   C.   Review And Approval Required:
      1.   If any waters or wastes are discharged or are proposed to be
discharged to the public sewers, which contain the substances enumerated in
subsection B2 of this section, and which, in the judgment of the Town agent,
may have a deleterious effect upon the sewage works, processes, equipment or
receiving waters, or which otherwise create a hazard to life or constitute a
public nuisance, the Town agent may: (2011 Code § 19-66; amd. 2017 Code)
         a.   Reject the wastes;
         b.   Require pretreatment to an acceptable condition for discharge to
the public sewers;
         c.   Require control over the quantities and rates of discharge; and/
or
         d.   Require payment to cover the added cost of handling and treating
the wastes not covered by existing taxes or sewer charges under the provisions
of section
9-5-6-6 of this chapter. (2011 Code § 19-66)
      2.   If the Town agent permits the pretreatment or equalization of waste
flows, the design and installation of the plants and equipment shall be subject
to the review and approval of the Town agent and subject to the requirements of
all applicable codes, ordinances and laws. (2011 Code § 19-66; amd. 2017 Code)
9-5-6-2: INTERCEPTORS:
Grease, oil and sand interceptors shall be provided when, in the opinion of the
Town agent, they are necessary for the proper handling of liquid wastes
containing grease in excessive amounts, or any flammable wastes, sand or other
harmful ingredients; except, that such interceptors shall not be required for
private living quarters or dwelling units. All interceptors shall be of a type
and capacity approved by the Town agent and shall be located as to be readily
and easily accessible for cleaning and inspection. (2011 Code § 19-67; amd.
2017 Code)
9-5-6-3: PRELIMINARY TREATMENT OR FLOW EQUALIZATION:
Where preliminary treatment or flow equalizing facilities are provided for any
waters or wastes, they shall be maintained continuously in satisfactory and
effective operation by the owner at his expense. (2011 Code § 19-68)
9-5-6-4: CONTROL MANHOLE:
When required by the Town agent, the owner of any property serviced by a
building sewer carrying industrial wastes shall install a suitable control
manhole, together with such necessary meters and other appurtenances, in the
building sewer to facilitate observation, sampling and measurement of the
wastes. Such manhole, when required, shall be accessible and safely located,
and shall be constructed in accordance with plans approved by the Town agent.
The manhole shall be installed by the owner at his expense and shall be
maintained by him so as to be safe and accessible at all times. (2011 Code §
19-69; amd. 2017 Code)
9-5-6-5: MEASUREMENTS, TESTS AND ANALYSES:
All measurements, tests and analyses of the characteristics of waters and
wastes to which reference is made in this section
9-5-6 shall be determined in accordance with the latest edition of "Standard
Methods for the Examination of Water and Wastewater", published by the American
Public Health Association, and shall be determined at the control manhole
provided in section
9-5-6-4 of this chapter, or upon suitable samples taken at the control manhole.
In the event that no special manhole has been required, the control manhole
shall be considered to be the nearest downstream manhole in the public sewer to
the point at which the building sewer is connected. Sampling shall be carried
out by customarily accepted methods to reflect the effect of constituents upon
the sewage works and to determine the existence of hazards to life, limb and
property. (The particular analyses involved will determine whether a 24 hour
composite of all outfalls of a premises is appropriate or whether a grab sample
or samples should be taken. Normally, but not always, BOD and suspended solids
analyses are obtained and determined from periodic grab samples.) (2011 Code §
19-70; amd. 2017 Code)
9-5-6-6: SPECIAL AGREEMENTS:
No statement contained in this section
9-5-6 shall be construed as preventing any special agreement or arrangement
between the Town and any industrial concern whereby industrial wastes, except
those that would be hazardous or would cause an upset of the treatment process
or that would interfere with the operation and maintenance of the collection
and/or treatment facilities, of unusual strength or character may be accepted
by the Town for treatment, subject to payment therefor by the industrial
concern in accordance with section
9-5-7 of this chapter. (2011 Code § 19-71)
9-5-7: USER CHARGES; INDUSTRIAL USERS:
   A.   User Charge: For the purpose of providing funds for the operation and
maintenance of the sanitary sewage system and for other purposes as allowed by
applicable law, there is hereby fixed and established a system of user charges
to be levied against each respective user thereof. The base level charges are
based on the costs of operation and maintenance of the sanitary sewerage
system, including replacement, as well as the volume, strength and delivery
flow rate of the sewage. The costs of treating the extraneous flows shall be
included in the operation and maintenance costs. The Town shall review the user
charges annually and revise them as necessary to reflect actual sanitary sewage
operation and maintenance costs among the users on January 1 of each calendar
year. The base level charge is comprised of a charge to service each account,
plus a volume charge for the normal strength sewage, plus a surcharge for
pollutants above normal strength. The Town shall maintain such records as are
necessary to document the adequacy and proportionality of the user charges. The
records shall be maintained as long as required by all applicable rules and
regulations. (Ord. 309, 8-11-2014; amd. 2017 Code)
      1.   Monthly Charge:
         a.   Established: The monthly volume of sewage discharge by each user
shall be assumed to be equal to the amount of water metered to the user, but in
cases where the volume cannot be reasonably determined to be so metered, the
amount of sewage shall be determined as provided in subsection F of this
section. The sewer rates shall be set and established by resolution of the
Board of Trustees of the Mooreland Public Works Authority and approved and
adopted by resolution of the Town Board of Trustees, and posted for inspection
in the Office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer, and shall apply equally to
residential and commercial users without maximum levels of charges to be
assessed. (Ord. 328, 3-13-2017; amd. 2017 Code)
         b.   Annual Fee Adjustment: Commencing July 1, 2017, and continuing
each subsequent July 1, the Board of Trustees shall review the fees charged and
shall recommend adjustment of the fees to the Town Board based upon the
percentage change in the consumer price index, all urban consumers, south
region, all items, during the twelve (12) month period ending in April
preceding the July in question. Any recommended change shall be rounded up to
the nearest nickel. (Ord. 328, 3-13-2017)
      2.   Surcharge System: A surcharge system meeting EPA requirements will
be developed if industries with above normal strength wastes and/or wastes
containing other pollutants that may increase the cost of operation and
maintenance desire to use the sewage facilities. There will be no "above normal
strength" charge nor will there be any reduction in the base level charge when
C is equal to or less than three hundred (300).
      3.   Sewage Analyses: The sewage shall be analyzed as discussed in
subsection B of this section, except the sewage from individual residences and
establishments known to discharge only domestic wastewater is assumed to be
normal strength and will not ordinarily be analyzed. The analysis will be
carried out in accordance with generally recognized methods. (2011 Code § 19-
60)
      4.   Computation Of Charge: The monthly "user charge", as defined in
section
9-5-2 of this chapter and referenced in this section starting with the second
billing following the effective date hereof, shall be computed according to the
formula and rates set and established by the Board of Trustees of the Mooreland
Public Works Authority, approved and adopted by the Town Board of Trustees by
resolution, and posted for inspection in the Office of the Town Clerk-
Treasurer. (2011 Code 19-60; amd. 2017 Code)
      5.   Use Of Sewer System But Not Water System: Except as herein otherwise
expressly provided, each person, firm, corporation, association, institution,
or establishment from whose property or premises sewage is discharged into the
sanitary sewage system of the Town, but who is not a water customer of the Town
and to pay a monthly user charge based upon the quantity of water thus metered
and the strength of sewage discharged, to be computed in like manner as
provided in this subsection.
      6.   Use Of Water System And Secondary Water System: Each user of the
sanitary sewerage system of the Town who is a water customer of the Town, but
who also obtains, uses or consumes water from any source other than from the
Town, is hereby required to meter, at such source, the quantity used, with an
appropriate meter to be approved by the Town, and to pay the monthly user
charge based upon the total quantity of water metered and the strength of
sewage discharged, to be computed in like manner as provided in this
subsection.
   B.   Industrial Cost Recovery (ICR): To be developed and adopted as required
by EPA prior to permitting use by a potentially affected industry.
   C.   Classification Of Industrial Users:
      1.   Minor Users: "Minor users" are those whose industrial discharge
meets all of the following criteria:
         a.   Flow: The maximum hourly rate of discharge, as defined in
subsection A2 of this section, is one thousand forty two (1,042) gallons or
less.
         b.   BOD And SS: Typical BOD and/or SS concentrations of the discharge
from similar industries do not exceed eighty percent (80%) of the values shown
for normal strength sewage in subs
9-5-6-1A2 of this chapter. The user will be classified as an intermediate or
major user if either value is exceeded more than ten percent (10%) of the time.
      2.   Intermediate Users: "Intermediate users" are those whose industrial
discharge exceeds the criteria for a minor user but does not exceed any of the
following criteria:
         a.   Flow: The maximum hourly rate of discharge, as previously
defined, does not exceed two thousand (2,000) gallons.
         b.   BOD And SS: The BOD and/or SS concentrations in the discharge do
not exceed one hundred percent (100%) of the values shown for normal strength
sewage in subs
9-5-6-1A2 of this chapter more than ten percent (10%) of the time.
      3.   Major Users: "Major users" are those whose industrial waste
discharge does not meet the flow, BOD or SS criteria listed for minor or
intermediate users. (2011 Code § 19-60)
   D.   Monitoring; Samples:
      1.   The BOD and SS concentrations in the discharge of minor users will
normally be determined from standard values for various industries established
by the Town agent. However, the Town agent will collect samples and may monitor
discharge rates on a random basis.
      2.   The intermediate users are required to cause a sample to be
collected and analyzed at least one (1) time per month.
      3.   The sample shall be made up of individual portions collected,
composited and analyzed so as to permit determination of the maximum hourly
discharge rates as previously defined. The analysis shall be determined and
certified by an independent testing laboratory employed by the user and
approved by the Town agent.
      4.   A report shall be prepared and submitted to the Town agent within
fifteen (15) working days after the sample is collected. The report shall be
signed and shall contain a statement assuring that the sample was collected and
composited in such a manner as to be representative of the maximum hourly
discharge rate. It shall include: (2011 Code § 19-60; amd. 2017 Code)
         a.   The starting and ending time of the sampling period; and
         b.   The hourly rate of flow observed during the sampling period; and
         c.   The concentrations of BOD and SS; and
         d.   The total pounds of BOD and SS discharged during the sampling
periods; and
         e.   The concentrations of other pollutants listed on the user's
current industrial discharge permit.
      5.   All costs associated with collection, compositing, analysis and
reporting of these samples shall be borne by the user.
      6.   The sampling point(s) shall be located, installed and maintained by
the user so that any authorized representative of the Town may readily and
safely obtain samples of the discharge during all hours when discharge occurs.
The Town can be expected to collect a grab sample one (1) or more times per
year from intermediate users and two (2) or more times per year from major
users. The Town may or may not give prior notice of its intent to collect a
sample(s). (2011 Code § 19-60)
   E.   Discharge Permits:
      1.   A user discharging industrial wastes into the sanitary sewerage
system prior to the effective date hereof may continue without penalty so long
as he does not increase the quantity of the discharge without the prior
permission of the Town agent, and has discharged the industrial waste at least
three (3) months prior to the effective date hereof, and applies for and is
granted a permit to discharge no later than one hundred twenty (120) days after
the effective date hereof. (2011 Code § 19-60; amd. 2017 Code)
      2.   Upon application on forms provided by the Town, a permit to
discharge may be granted to users; provided, that the user:
         a.   Submits an application within forty five (45) days after the
effective date hereof; and (2011 Code § 19-60)
         b.   Secures approval by the Town agent of plans and specifications
for pretreatment facilities when required; and (2011 Code § 19-60; amd. 2017
Code)
         c.   Has complied with all requirements including, but not limited to:
            (1)   Payment of charges; and
            (2)   Installation and operation of pretreatment facilities when
required; and
            (3)   Sampling and analyses to determine quantity and quality.
      3.   A person applying for a new discharge shall:
         a.   Meet all conditions of subsection A of this section except
subsection A1 of this section; and
         b.   Submit an application for discharge sixty (60) days or more prior
to the planned initiation of such discharge; and
         c.   Secure a permit to discharge prior to discharging any wastes; and
         d.   Demonstrate compliance with applicable State and Federal
Statutes, rules and regulations. (2011 Code § 19-60)
      4.   Permits issued under this subsection E are issued subject to
conditions listed thereon and all other applicable local, State and Federal
Statutes, rules and regulations. The permits are subject to revocation for
noncompliance. The permit conditions are subject to modification by the Town
agent if such modification is or becomes necessary to protect the sanitary
sewerage system or its proper functioning, or if such modification becomes
necessary as a result of requirements imposed by the State or Federal
government. (2011 Code § 19-60; amd. 2017 Code)
   F.   Right To Have Charges Reviewed: Any person, firm, corporation,
association, institution, or establishment from whose property or premises
sewage is discharged into the sanitary sewerage system of the Town, where the
charges, as determined in accordance with the provisions of this section, do
not reasonably reflect the amount of sewage and concentration of BOD and/or
suspended solids discharged by the applicant into the sanitary sewerage system,
may apply in writing to the Town Board to make a survey of the special facts
and conditions shown to exist by such application. After considering such
application and survey, the Town Board shall determine the amount of sewage and
concentration of BOD and suspended solids discharged by the applicant into the
sanitary sewer system under the special facts and conditions shown to exist so
that the charges to the applicant will be just, fair and equitable. (2011 Code
§ 19-61)
   G.   Disconnection Of Service: The Town may terminate water and wastewater
disposal service and disconnect an industrial customer from the system when:
      1.   Acids or chemicals damaging to sewer lines or treatment processes
are released to the sewer, causing rapid deterioration of these structures or
interfering with proper conveyance and treatment of wastewater.
      2.   A governmental agency informs the Town that the effluent from the
wastewater treatment plant is no longer of a quality permitted for discharge to
a watercourse, and it is found that the customer is delivering wastewater to
the Municipal system that cannot be sufficiently treated or requires treatment
that is not provided as normal domestic treatment. (2011 Code § 11-2)
      3.   The customer:
         a.   Discharges waste or wastewater that is in violation of the permit
issued by the Town agent. (2011 Code § 11-2; amd. 2017 Code)
         b.   Discharges wastewater at an uncontrolled, variable rate in
sufficient quantity to cause an imbalance in the wastewater treatment system.
         c.   Fails to pay monthly bills for water and sanitary sewer services
when due.
         d.   Repeats a discharge of prohibited wastes to the public sewer.
(2011 Code § 11-2)
9-5-8: USERS OUTSIDE TOWN LIMITS:
Each user of the sanitary sewerage system of the Town whose property or
premises may be located outside the corporate limits of the Town shall pay as a
sewer service charge a sum as set and established by resolution of the Board of
Trustees of the Mooreland Public Works Authority and approved and adopted by
resolution of the Town Board of Trustees, and posted for inspection in the
Office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer. The Town does not obligate itself to
furnish sanitary sewer service to any persons whomsoever, but will furnish such
service as is reasonable within its financial ability to do so. (2011 Code §
19-61; amd. 2017 Code)
9-5-9: TAMPERING WITH, DAMAGING SYSTEM:
No unauthorized person shall maliciously, wilfully or negligently break,
damage, destroy, uncover, deface or tamper with any structure, appurtenance or
equipment which is a part of the sewage works. Any person violating this
section shall be subject to immediate arrest under the charge of disorderly
conduct. (2011 Code § 19-72)
9-5-10: POWERS AND AUTHORITY OF INSPECTORS:
   A.   1. The plumbing inspector and other duly authorized employees of the
Town bearing proper credentials and identification shall be permitted to enter
all properties for the purpose of inspection, observation, measurement,
sampling and testing in accordance with the provisions of this chapter. The
plumbing inspector or his representatives shall have no authority to inquire
into any processes including metallurgical, chemical, oil, refining, ceramic,
paper or other industries beyond that point having a direct bearing on the kind
and source of discharge to the sewers or waterways or facilities for waste
treatment.
      2.   While performing the necessary work on private properties referred
to in subsection A1 of this section, the plumbing inspector or duly authorized
employees of the Town shall observe all safety rules applicable to the premises
established by the company, and the company shall be held harmless for injury
or death to the Town employees, and the Town shall indemnify the company
against loss or damage to its property by Town employees and against liability
claims and demands for personal injury or property damage asserted against the
company and growing out of the gauging and sampling operation, except as such
may be caused by negligence or failure of the company to maintain safe
conditions.
   B.   The plumbing inspector and other duly authorized employees of the Town
bearing proper credentials and identification shall be permitted to enter all
private properties through which the Town holds a duly negotiated easement for
the purposes of, but not limited to, inspection, observation, measurement,
sampling, repair and maintenance of any portion of the sewage works lying
within said easement. All entry and subsequent work, if any, on said easement
shall be done in full accordance with the terms of the duly negotiated easement
pertaining to the private property involved. (2011 Code § 19-73)
9-5-11: VIOLATIONS; PENALTIES:
   A.   Notice Of Violation: Any person found to be violating any provisions of
this chapter shall be served by the Town with written notice stating the nature
of the violation and providing a reasonable time limit for the satisfactory
correction thereof. The offender shall, within the period of time stated in
such notice, permanently cease all violations.
   B.   Misdemeanor Violation; Penalty: Any person who shall continue any
violation beyond the time limit provided in subsection A of this section shall
be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be punishable as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. Each day on which any such violation shall continue shall
be deemed a separate offense.
   C.   Liability For Costs: Any person violating any of the provisions of this
chapter shall become liable to the Town for any expense, loss or damage
occasioned the Town by reason of such violation. (2011 Code § 19-74)
CHAPTER 6
GARBAGE AND REFUSE COLLECTION AND DISPOSAL
SECTION:
9-6-1: Definitions
9-6-2: Accumulations, Deposits Prohibited
9-6-3: Right To Contract For Collection And Disposal
9-6-4: Preparation Of Garbage And Refuse, Receptacle Specifications And Use Of
Receptacles
9-6-4-1: Dumpster Rentals
9-6-5: Rates; Billing And Delinquent Payments
9-6-6: Sale Or Removal Of Garbage And Refuse By Business Owners Permitted
9-6-7: Violation; Penalty
9-6-1: DEFINITIONS:
The following words and phrases, as used in this chapter, are deemed to have
the definitions in this section unless a contrary meaning is clearly evident:
BUSINESS SECTION: The business section of the Town of Mooreland shall refer to
the fire limits of the Town.
GARBAGE: All refuse or animal and vegetable matter or food products from
kitchens, pantries, and dining rooms of hotels, residences, restaurants,
boarding houses, apartment houses, and meat markets.
RECEPTACLES: Waterproof cans with close fitting covers not exceeding thirty
(30) gallons in capacity or sanitary refuse boxes approved by the State
Department of Health.
TRASH: Ashes, cinders, papers, rags, tin cans, bottles, and other substances
which may accumulate. (2011 Code § 11-1)
9-6-2: ACCUMULATIONS, DEPOSITS PROHIBITED:
   A.   Accumulation:
      1.   It is hereby declared unlawful in the Town for any person, firm or
corporation to permit trash or other refuse to scatter from the property owned,
leased or occupied by such person, firm or corporation onto the streets and
alleys of the Town or onto the properties of others.
      2.   It is hereby declared unlawful in the Town for any person, firm or
corporation to permit trash or other refuse to accumulate, pile up and become
unsightly on the property owned, leased, or occupied by such person, firm or
corporation. (2011 Code § 11-26)
   B.   Deposits: No garbage or trash shall be thrown or dropped upon any
street, avenue, or alley. (2011 Code § 11-27)
9-6-3: RIGHT TO CONTRACT FOR COLLECTION AND DISPOSAL:
The Town shall have the right to enter into contract and agreement with the
County for the acquisition, management and operation of landfill facilities for
disposal of solid waste and other refuse, to collect, remove, and dispose of,
and to provide for the collection, removal and disposal of, all garbage and
trash within the limits of the Town, either by contract with some suitable
person for the removal of such garbage or by removing the same by Town
employees at the discretion of the Town. (2011 Code § 11-22)
9-6-4: PREPARATION OF GARBAGE AND REFUSE, RECEPTACLE SPECIFICATIONS AND USE OF
RECEPTACLES:
Garbage and trash hauling services, when provided by the Town, shall be
provided only under the following rules and regulations: (2011 Code § 11-25)
   A.   Preparation Of Garbage And Refuse; Prohibited Materials:
      1.   All garbage and refuse containing animal or vegetable matter and
also commonly known as "household kitchen trash" shall be bagged and placed in
a Town approved receptacle.
      2.   No grass shall be placed in any receptacle unless grass cuttings are
first bagged. (2011 Code § 11-27)
      3.   a. Building materials, trees, brush and scrap iron or steel are not
hauled by the Town. The hauling of such items is the responsibility of the
owner thereof. (2011 Code § 11-25)
         b.   Tree limbs, bricks, stones, mortar, shingles, lumber, iron, and
steel products, used furniture and household appliances shall not be placed in
any Town receptacle. (2011 Code § 11-27)
   B.   Receptacle Specifications: Metal, plastic and/or fiberglass containers
with handles, not to exceed thirty (30) gallons nor more than fifty (50) pounds
when fully loaded, must be provided for trash and garbage by those who desire
the service. A sufficient number of containers must be provided for one week's
accumulation. Watertight lids must be in place on all containers.
   C.   Location Of Containers For Pick Up:
      1.   In all areas of the Town where there are open unobstructed alleys or
easements wide enough and improved enough for collection vehicles to travel
with ease, garbage and trash containers will be placed on the alley or easement
property line for pick up; except, that they may be placed in a platted alley
if they do not interfere with traffic through the alley.
      2.   In areas where alleys or easements, as described herein, do not
exist, collection will be made from the street. It is the responsibility of
those wanting trash service to place containers on the curb in front of the
residence or in a location easily accessible and clearly visible to the
collectors (not more than 10 feet from the curb) on those days when pick up is
scheduled. The residents will be responsible to remove their trash containers
from the curb after trash pick up so as not to create an unsightly nuisance for
the Town.
   D.   Pick Up Schedule: All garbage and trash collections shall be made by
the Town at stipulated times as prescribed by the rules of the Mayor or his
designee.
   E.   Maintenance Of Receptacles; Noncompliance With Provisions:
      1.   It shall be the duty of the owner of garbage cans to keep them clean
at any and all times and to maintain them in a sanitary condition, as well as
the grounds around the same.
      2.   Any container that does not conform to the provisions of this
section or that may be ragged or sharp edged or any other defect liable to
hamper or injure the person collecting the contents thereof shall be promptly
replaced upon notice.
      3.   The Town shall have the authority to refuse collection services for
failure to comply with this chapter. (2011 Code § 11-25)
   F.   Use Of Another's Trash Container: It shall be unlawful for any person
to use another person's trash container, whether the container is furnished by
the Town or by the individual, without permission of such other person. (Ord.
338, 6-11-2018)
9-6-4-1: DUMPSTER RENTALS:
   A.   Rental Requirements: Citizens of the Town can rent a dumpster from the
Town for a maximum of three (3) days with one dump for a fee set and
established by resolution of the Board of Trustees of the Mooreland Public
Works Authority and approved and adopted by resolution of the Town Board of
Trustees, and posted for inspection in the Office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer.
The dumpster will be delivered on Friday and will be picked up and dumped on
Tuesday. (2011 Code § 11-23; amd. 2017 Code)
   B.   Prohibited Materials: The following items cannot be put into the
dumpster: any type of appliances, pipe, cable, wire, wire rope (includes
barbwire), tree limbs not longer than four feet (4'), tires, car batteries,
ashes, rocks, dirt, cement, building materials of any kind, dead carcasses,
cans of paint, paint thinner or acids of any kind. (2011 Code § 11-23)
   C.   Overfill Costs: The dumpster can only be filled to the top. If the
dumpster is overfilled or too heavy to be dumped, it will not be emptied, and
there will be a penalty and weekly fee, until the renter has emptied the
overflow and the dumpster can be removed, as set and established by resolution
of the Board of Trustees of the Mooreland Public Works Authority and approved
and adopted by resolution of the Town Board of Trustees, and posted for
inspection in the Office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer. (2011 Code § 11-23; amd.
2017 Code)
9-6-5: RATES; BILLING AND DELINQUENT PAYMENTS:
   A.   Rates Established:
      1.   The trash and/or garbage rates in the Town are as set and
established by resolution of the Board of Trustees of the Mooreland Public
Works Authority and approved and adopted by resolution of the Town Board of
Trustees, and posted for inspection in the Office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer.
(Ord. 330, 3-13-2017; amd. 2017 Code)
      2.   Commencing July 1, 2017, and continuing each subsequent July 1, the
Board of Trustees shall review the fees charged and shall recommend adjustment
of the fees to the Town Board based upon the percentage change in the Consumer
Price Index, All Urban Consumers, South Region, All Items, during the twelve
(12) month period ending in April preceding the July in question. Any
recommended change shall be rounded up to the nearest nickel. (Ord. 330, 3-13-
2017)
   B.   Bills For Service; Delinquencies:
      1.   The Town Clerk-Treasurer is hereby authorized and directed to
collect the fees for garbage and refuse collection and disposal from the owners
and/or occupants of the various premises within the corporate limits of the
Town, on a monthly basis, payable between the first and tenth of each month.
(2011 Code § 11-23; amd. 2017 Code)
      2.   The fees for the removal of garbage and/or trash shall be billed to
each owner or occupant liable therefor with the water bill where said owner or
occupant is a water user unless such user is a commercial business and receives
trash services other than from the Town. (2011 Code § 11-23)
      3.   A delinquency charge of ten percent (10%) shall be added to any bill
for the removal of garbage or trash which has not been paid within ten (10)
days from the due date stated on the bill. (2011 Code § 11-24)
      4.   Fees for water service will not be accepted without payment of the
fees for removal of trash and/or garbage, and failure to pay the said charge
for the removal of trash or garbage, when due, shall be cause for
discontinuance of either water service or garbage and trash collection, or
both. (2011 Code § 11-23)
9-6-6: SALE OR REMOVAL OF GARBAGE AND REFUSE BY BUSINESS OWNERS PERMITTED:
This chapter does not prevent owners or occupants in the business section from
selling or removing garbage of value from hotels, restaurants, and boarding
houses. In that event, garbage shall be removed in covered metal containers and
handled in such manner so as that in the removal thereof, no such garbage shall
be spilled or dropped onto any streets, avenues, alleys or sidewalks. The
containers for garbage shall be approved by the Town. (2011 Code § 11-28)
9-6-7: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person, firm or corporation violating any provisions of this chapter shall
be guilty of a misdemeanor and, upon conviction thereof, shall be punishable as
provided in section
1-4-1 of this Code. In addition thereto, such person may be enjoined from
continuing such violations. Each day a violation is allowed to exist is a
separate offense. (2011 Code § 11-30)
CHAPTER 2
TERMS AND CONDITIONS OF UTILITY SERVICES
ARTICLE C. FRAUDULENT USE OF SERVICES
SECTION:
9-2C-1: Definition
9-2C-2: Fraudulent Use Of Services
9-2C-3: Tampering With Utility Equipment Or Property
9-2C-1: DEFINITION:
For the purpose of this article, the term "fraudulent use of service" shall
include any unauthorized use of the Town's electric, sewer, water and garbage
services and facilities by the consumer. (2011 Code § 19-117; amd. 2017 Code)
9-2C-2: FRAUDULENT USE OF SERVICES:
In the event fraudulent use of a service or evidence of attempted fraudulent
use of a service is discovered, or where the Town's regulating or measuring
equipment or other property has been tampered with, service(s) may be
disconnected by the Town without advance notice to the consumer. Service to the
consumer will not be resumed until the consumer shall have paid all bills
including:
   A.   The charge for the estimated amount of service fraudulently consumed.
   B.   The cost of replacement or repair of any damaged meter or associated
equipment. (2011 Code § 19-117)
   C.   A reconnection charge set and established by resolution of the Board of
Trustees of the Mooreland Public Works Authority and approved and adopted by
resolution of the Town Board of Trustees, and posted for inspection in the
Office of the Town Clerk- Treasurer. (2011 Code § 19-117; amd. 2017 Code)
   D.   If service has been restored by other than Town personnel after having
been disconnected initially for one (1) of the reasons stated herein, the
consumer shall, in addition to the charges enumerated above, pay a charge set
and established by the Board of Trustees of the Mooreland Public Works
Authority and approved and adopted by the Town Board of Trustees, and posted
for inspection in the Office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer.
   E.   If it has been shown to the satisfaction of the Town that the consumer
or applicant for service had no connection with or knowledge of such fraudulent
use of service(s) or such tampering, service may be resumed after the condition
causing or permitting the fraudulent usage has been corrected and such consumer
or applicant for service has paid for any unmetered service received. (2011
Code § 19-117)
9-2C-3: TAMPERING WITH UTILITY EQUIPMENT OR PROPERTY:
No regulating or measuring equipment or other property or equipment owned by
the Town, wherever situated, whether upon the consumer's premises or elsewhere,
shall be tampered with or interfered with for the purpose of adjustment,
fraudulent adjustment or otherwise. In the event equipment has been tampered
with, the Town will follow the same procedures as for fraudulent use of
services as outlined in section
9-2C-2 of this article. (2011 Code § 19-118)
TITLE 10
BUILDING REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
ENFORCEMENT; APPEALS; PENALTY
SECTION:
10-1-1: Building Official
10-1-2: Appeals
10-1-3: Violation; Penalty
10-1-4: Injunctions; Relief In Courts
10-1-1: BUILDING OFFICIAL:
The Town building official shall be appointed by the Town Board of Trustees and
shall have the powers and duties prescribed for the building official by the
Town Building Codes; provided, that his powers and duties may by exercised by
his authorized representative under his supervision and control. The term
"building inspector", "plumbing inspector" and "gas inspector", wherever used
in this Code and the ordinances of the Town, also each refer to and mean the
building official, unless a separate electrical inspector, plumbing inspector,
or gas inspector is appointed by the Town Board of Trustees. (2011 Code § 4-4)
10-1-2: APPEALS:
Any person aggrieved of any officer, department, board or agency of the Town
affected by any decision or interpretation of the building official in
connection with the interpretation of any of the provisions of this title may
appeal to the Town Board of Adjustment, which shall be the Town Trustees;
provided, that: (2011 Code § 4-7)
   A.   Such appeal shall be taken within ten (10) days from the date of
decision by filing with the building official and the Town Clerk-Treasurer a
written notice of appeal specifying the grounds thereof and by paying a filing
fee as provided in the fee schedule adopted by resolution of the Town Board of
Trustees at the Office of the Town Clerk-Treasurer at the time the notice is
filed. (2011 Code § 4-7; amd. 2017 Code)
   B.   The Town Clerk-Treasurer, upon receipt of the notice of appeal, shall
transmit to the Board of Adjustment the papers and information constituting the
record upon which the action appealed from was taken.
   C.   The Board of Adjustment shall fix a time for hearing of appeal. It
shall give written notice to the parties in interest at least five (5) days
before the date set for the hearing. Such notice shall contain the date, the
hour and the place for the hearing. The Board of Adjustment will also post
notice of the date, time and place of the hearing in two (2) public places
within the Town. Upon the hearing, parties in interest may appear in person or
by agent or attorneys. (2011 Code § 4-7)
10-1-3: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
Any person, firm or corporation who shall engage in any business, trade or
vocation for which a license, permit or certificate of registration is required
by this title, without having a valid license, permit or certificate of
registration as required, or who shall fail to do anything required by this
title or by any Code adopted by this title, or who shall otherwise violate any
provision of this title or of any Code adopted by this title, or who shall
